    How This Course Works

    Each lab follows a consistent pattern:

    1. Why This Matters — context for the exam concept
    2. See It In Action — an interactive Claude Code demonstration of the concept
    3. Reference Implementation — production code to study (this is what the exam tests)
    4. Try It — ask Claude Code to create and run the code for you
    5. Code Analysis — comprehension questions to test your understanding
    6. Checkpoint — verify you've grasped the key patterns

    You follow along step by step in Claude Code. When a lab has reference code, you can ask Claude Code to create the file and run it — Claude Code handles dependencies and API access automatically.

    Troubleshooting — Common Issues

    1. Claude Code not connecting: Run claude /doctor to diagnose. Check that your subscription is active.

    2. Python version: Some labs use Python scripts. Requires Python 3.8+. Check with python --version. If you have python3 instead of python, use python3 throughout.

    3. Dependencies not installed: When Claude Code runs a Python script for you, ask it to install any missing packages. For example: "Install the anthropic package and then run the script."

    4. Permission denied on .sh files: Run chmod +x filename.sh before executing bash scripts.

    5. Claude Code not recognizing CLAUDE.md: Restart Claude Code after creating/modifying CLAUDE.md files. Use /memory to verify what's loaded.

    6. Labs produce different output than expected: Claude's responses vary between runs. Focus on the STRUCTURE (stop_reason values, error categories, tool calls) not exact text.

    MODULE 1: AGENTIC ARCHITECTURE & ORCHESTRATION

    Domain 1 — 27% of exam Task Statements 1.1 – 1.7

    Key Terms for Module 1

    Before diving in, here are the core terms you'll use throughout this module:

    • Agentic loop: A while-loop in your code where Claude keeps running until the task is done. Each iteration: send request → check stop_reason → execute tools or return response.
    • stop_reason: Claude's signal telling your code what to do next. "tool_use" = "I need you to run these tools and give me the results." "end_turn" = "I'm done, here's my final answer."
    • tool_use: A content block in Claude's response containing a tool call (tool name + input). Your code must execute it and send the result back.
    • tool_result: Your response feeding the tool's output back to Claude as a role: "user" message.
    • Hub-and-spoke: Architecture where one coordinator agent manages all communication. Subagents only talk to the coordinator, never to each other.
    • Coordinator: The central agent that decides which subagents to invoke, passes context, and aggregates results.
    • Subagent: A specialized agent that handles one part of a task (e.g., search, analysis, synthesis). Has isolated context — doesn't automatically know what other subagents found.
    • Task tool: The Agent SDK mechanism for spawning subagents. The coordinator must have "Task" in its allowedTools.
    • AgentDefinition: Configuration for a subagent: name, description, system_prompt, and allowed_tools.
    • Prerequisite gate: Code that blocks a tool call until a prior step has completed (e.g., can't refund until customer is verified).
    • PostToolUse / PreToolUse hooks: Functions that intercept tool calls. PostToolUse transforms results AFTER execution. PreToolUse blocks calls BEFORE execution.
    • Prompt chaining: Fixed sequential pipeline — steps are always the same regardless of input.
    • Dynamic decomposition: Adaptive pipeline — next steps depend on what was discovered in prior steps.
    • fork_session: Creates independent exploration branches from a shared analysis baseline.
    • --resume: CLI flag to continue a named session from where you left off.

    LAB 1.1: BUILD A REAL AGENTIC LOOP

    Domain 1 — Task Statement 1.1 stop_reason lifecycle, tool results, anti-patterns ~30 minutesGuided | Requires: Claude Code

    Why This Matters

    Every agent you'll ever build — customer support, code review, research — runs on the same core loop. If you get this wrong, your agent either hangs forever, exits too early, or loses tool results. This lab is the foundation for everything else in the certification. 27% of exam questions trace back to this pattern.

    The problem it solves: Claude can't run tools by itself. It can only ask your code to run them. Your code needs a loop that keeps going until Claude says "I'm done." That signal is stop_reason.

    How the Agentic Loop Works

    Think of it like a conversation between your code and Claude:

    1. Your code sends the question + tool definitions to Claude
    2. Claude analyzes and decides: "Do I need a tool to answer this?"
    3. If yes: Claude returns stop_reason="tool_use" — meaning "I need you to run these tools and send me the results"
    4. Your code executes those tools and sends results back as role: "user" messages
    5. If no (task is done): Claude returns stop_reason="end_turn" — meaning "I'm done, here's my final answer"

    This loop continues until stop_reason="end_turn". That's the entire pattern.

    The two things that can go wrong:

    • You check for the wrong termination signal (e.g., parsing text instead of stop_reason) → agent exits mid-task
    • You forget to send tool results back as role: "user" → Claude never gets the data it asked for

    See It In Action

    Open Claude Code and try this:

    I'm jane@email.com. Can you look up my customer record and then check on order ORD-555?

    Watch what happens in the output. Claude Code will:

    1. Call a tool to look up the customer by email
    2. Receive the result and process it
    3. Call another tool to look up the order
    4. Receive that result and compose a final response

    Each tool call is one iteration of the agentic loop. The loop continues until Claude has all the information it needs — that's the stop_reason: "end_turn" signal.

    Challenge Mode (optional — try before looking at the reference)

    Build it yourself first. Before reading the code below, ask Claude Code:

    Build me a Python script with a while True agentic loop. It should:
- Define two tools: get_customer (by email) and lookup_order (by order_id) with fake data
- Send a user message that requires both tools
- Loop checking stop_reason: "tool_use" means execute tools, "end_turn" means done
- Print each iteration showing the stop_reason value

    Then compare Claude Code's implementation to the reference below.

    Reference Implementation: lab-d1-agentic-arch/basic_loop.py

    import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

CUSTOMERS = {
    "jane@email.com": {"id": "CUST-001", "name": "Jane Smith", "tier": "gold"},
    "bob@email.com":  {"id": "CUST-002", "name": "Bob Jones",  "tier": "silver"}
}
ORDERS = {
    "ORD-555": {"id": "ORD-555", "customer_id": "CUST-001",
                "items": ["Blue Widget x2"], "total": 149.99,
                "status": "shipped", "tracking": "1Z999AA10123456784"},
    "ORD-777": {"id": "ORD-777", "customer_id": "CUST-002",
                "items": ["Green Thing x1"], "total": 29.99,
                "status": "processing", "tracking": None}
}

def execute_tool(name, input_data):
    if name == "get_customer":
        c = CUSTOMERS.get(input_data.get("email", ""))
        return json.dumps(c) if c else json.dumps({"error": "No customer found"})
    if name == "lookup_order":
        o = ORDERS.get(input_data.get("order_id", ""))
        return json.dumps(o) if o else json.dumps({"error": "Order not found"})
    return json.dumps({"error": f"Unknown tool: {name}"})

tools = [
    {
        "name": "get_customer",
        "description": (
            "Retrieves customer information by email address. "
            "Input: email (string). Returns: customer ID, name, tier. "
            "Use this to verify identity before any order operations."
        ),
        "input_schema": {"type": "object",
                         "properties": {"email": {"type": "string"}},
                         "required": ["email"]}
    },
    {
        "name": "lookup_order",
        "description": (
            "Retrieves order details by order ID (e.g. 'ORD-555'). "
            "Returns: status, items, total, tracking. "
            "Use when a customer asks about a specific order."
        ),
        "input_schema": {"type": "object",
                         "properties": {"order_id": {"type": "string"}},
                         "required": ["order_id"]}
    }
]

def run_agent(user_message):
    print(f"\n{'='*60}\nUSER: {user_message}\n{'='*60}\n")
    messages = [{"role": "user", "content": user_message}]
    iteration = 0

    while True:
        iteration += 1
        print(f"--- Loop iteration {iteration} ---")

        response = client.messages.create(
            model="claude-sonnet-4-6",
            max_tokens=1024,
            tools=tools,
            messages=messages
        )

        # ┌──────────────────────────────────────┐
        # │  stop_reason is the ONLY loop signal  │
        # └──────────────────────────────────────┘
        print(f"    stop_reason: {response.stop_reason}")

        if response.stop_reason == "end_turn":
            text = "".join(b.text for b in response.content if hasattr(b, "text"))
            print(f"\nAGENT RESPONSE:\n{text}\n")
            return text

        elif response.stop_reason == "tool_use":
            messages.append({"role": "assistant", "content": response.content})
            tool_results = []
            for block in response.content:
                if block.type == "tool_use":
                    print(f"    Tool call: {block.name}({json.dumps(block.input)})")
                    result = execute_tool(block.name, block.input)
                    print(f"    Result: {result[:80]}...")
                    tool_results.append({
                        "type": "tool_result",
                        "tool_use_id": block.id,
                        "content": result
                    })
            messages.append({"role": "user", "content": tool_results})
        else:
            break

if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_agent("I'm jane@email.com, can you check on my order ORD-555?")
    run_agent("I'm unknown@email.com, where's my order?")

    Try It

    Ask Claude Code to create and run this file:

    Create the file lab-d1-agentic-arch/basic_loop.py with the code above and run it

    What you should see: iteration 1 → stop_reason: tool_use → iteration 2 → stop_reason: tool_use → iteration 3 → stop_reason: end_turn. The loop terminates only when Claude returns end_turn.

    Exam connection (Sample Q1 pattern): This loop pattern — checking stop_reason, not parsing text — is the foundation. Every wrong answer on loop termination uses text parsing or arbitrary iteration caps.

    Code Analysis

    Exercise 1 — What breaks if you remove tool result appending? Look at line messages.append({"role": "user", "content": tool_results}). If this line is removed, Claude never receives the tool output it asked for. It will either error or hallucinate a response. The tool results MUST be sent back as role: "user" messages.

    Exercise 2 — Why is text-parsing an anti-pattern? Consider replacing the stop_reason check with:

    # ANTI-PATTERN — never do this
text = "".join(b.text for b in response.content if hasattr(b, "text"))
if len(text) > 50:
    break

    This exits the loop whenever Claude's text response exceeds 50 characters — even in the middle of tool calls. It ignores stop_reason entirely. This is why stop_reason is the only correct termination mechanism.

    Exercise 3 — How many loop iterations for the jane@email.com query? Trace through the code: iteration 1 calls get_customer, iteration 2 calls lookup_order, iteration 3 returns the final response with stop_reason: "end_turn". Answer: 3 iterations.

    Exam Essentials

    • If the exam says "agent exits mid-task" → answer involves stop_reason, NOT text parsing or iteration caps
    • Wrong answer trap: "Set a maximum iteration count" — caps are a safety net, not a termination strategy
    • Wrong answer trap: "Check if response contains a final answer" — text parsing misses tool-call iterations
    • The correct pattern: stop_reason == "end_turn" is the only valid loop termination signal

    ✅ Lab 1.1 Checkpoint

    • stop_reason "tool_use" → execute tools → loop continues
    • stop_reason "end_turn" → extract text → loop terminates
    • Tool results MUST be appended as role "user" with type "tool_result"
    • Never parse text content to detect loop completion

    LAB 1.2: MULTI-AGENT COORDINATOR

    Domain 1 — Task Statement 1.2 Hub-and-spoke, isolated context, dynamic subagent selection ~25 minutesIntermediate | Requires: Claude Code

    Quick Recall (from previous labs)

    1. What is the ONLY valid signal for loop termination in an agentic loop? (Lab 1.1)
    2. What happens if you forget to append tool results as role: "user"? (Lab 1.1)

    Why This Matters

    The problem: A single agent with 15 tools gets confused — it picks the wrong tool, forgets context, and produces shallow results. The solution: split the work across specialized agents, each with 3-4 tools and a focused prompt.

    But this creates a new problem: subagents can't see each other's work. If your search agent finds 3 articles and your analysis agent needs those articles, someone has to pass them explicitly. That "someone" is the coordinator — a central agent that decides who works on what and routes context between them.

    Exam connection (Sample Q7): When a multi-agent report misses entire topics, the root cause is almost always the coordinator's task decomposition being too narrow — not a subagent failure.

    What You'll Learn

    • The hub-and-spoke pattern: coordinator talks to all subagents, subagents never talk to each other
    • Why context is isolated by default (and why that's a feature, not a bug)
    • How the coordinator decides which subagents to invoke dynamically

    See It In Action

    Open Claude Code and try this:

    Research the current state of electric vehicle adoption. First search for recent market data, then analyze regional differences, then synthesize everything into a summary with sources cited.

    Watch how Claude Code breaks this into distinct phases — searching, analyzing, and synthesizing. Each phase uses different capabilities, and Claude Code must carry context forward explicitly. This is the hub-and-spoke pattern: one coordinator (Claude Code) managing specialized tasks that don't automatically share context with each other.

    Reference Implementation: lab-d1-agentic-arch/multi_agent.py

    import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

# ── SIMULATED SUBAGENT RESPONSES ──────────────────────────
# In production these would be real API calls to specialized agents.
# We simulate them here to focus on the coordinator pattern.

def search_subagent(query: str) -> dict:
    """Simulates a web search subagent."""
    print(f"  [SEARCH AGENT] Searching: '{query}'")
    # Simulated results
    return {
        "agent": "search",
        "query": query,
        "findings": [
            {"claim": "Global EV market grew 35% in 2023", "source": "https://iea.org/ev-report-2024", "date": "2024-01"},
            {"claim": "Battery costs fell to $139/kWh in 2023", "source": "https://bnef.com/battery-survey", "date": "2024-02"},
        ],
        "coverage": "high",
        "gaps": []
    }

def analysis_subagent(document: str, question: str) -> dict:
    """Simulates a document analysis subagent."""
    print(f"  [ANALYSIS AGENT] Analyzing document for: '{question}'")
    return {
        "agent": "analysis",
        "question": question,
        "findings": [
            {"claim": "EV adoption varies significantly by region", "source": "internal-doc", "confidence": 0.9},
            {"claim": "Charging infrastructure remains the top barrier", "source": "internal-doc", "confidence": 0.85},
        ],
        "coverage": "medium",
        "gaps": ["policy incentives not covered in document"]
    }

def synthesis_subagent(search_results: dict, analysis_results: dict, topic: str) -> str:
    """Simulates a synthesis subagent that combines findings from other agents.

    KEY PATTERN: All prior findings are passed explicitly in the prompt.
    The synthesis agent does NOT inherit context from previous calls.
    """
    print(f"  [SYNTHESIS AGENT] Synthesizing findings for: '{topic}'")

    # In production: call Claude API with ALL prior findings explicitly in the prompt
    # The prompt would look like:
    # """
    # Topic: {topic}
    #
    # Web Search Findings (from search agent):
    # {json.dumps(search_results, indent=2)}
    #
    # Document Analysis Findings (from analysis agent):
    # {json.dumps(analysis_results, indent=2)}
    #
    # Synthesize these findings into a comprehensive report.
    # Preserve all source attributions.
    # """

    # Simulate synthesis output with preserved attributions
    all_claims = search_results["findings"] + analysis_results["findings"]
    return json.dumps({
        "synthesis": f"Research on '{topic}' from {len(all_claims)} sources",
        "key_findings": all_claims,
        "coverage_gaps": search_results["gaps"] + analysis_results["gaps"],
        "sources_preserved": len(all_claims)
    })


# ── COORDINATOR ──────────────────────────────────────────
# The coordinator: analyzes query → selects subagents → aggregates results

def coordinator(query: str):
    """
    Hub-and-spoke coordinator pattern.

    Responsibilities:
    1. Analyze query to determine which subagents are needed
    2. Invoke selected subagents (sometimes in parallel)
    3. Pass ALL prior findings explicitly when invoking synthesis
    4. Evaluate synthesis for gaps → re-delegate if needed
    """
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print(f"COORDINATOR: Processing query: '{query}'")
    print(f"{'='*60}")

    # Step 1: Determine which subagents are needed
    # (Simple heuristic here; in production, use Claude to decide)
    needs_search = "market" in query.lower() or "trend" in query.lower()
    needs_analysis = "document" in query.lower() or "report" in query.lower() or True  # always analyze

    print(f"\nStep 1: Subagent selection")
    print(f"  Needs search agent:   {needs_search}")
    print(f"  Needs analysis agent: {needs_analysis}")

    # Step 2: Invoke selected subagents
    # In production: emit multiple Task tool calls in a SINGLE coordinator response
    # for parallel execution. Sequential calls here for clarity.
    search_results = None
    analysis_results = None

    if needs_search:
        search_results = search_subagent(query)

    if needs_analysis:
        analysis_results = analysis_subagent("sample document content", query)

    # Step 3: Invoke synthesis with ALL prior findings explicitly passed
    # THIS IS THE KEY: subagents don't share memory, so we pass everything
    print(f"\nStep 2: Passing {len((search_results or {}).get('findings', [])) + len((analysis_results or {}).get('findings', []))} findings to synthesis")

    synthesis = synthesis_subagent(
        search_results or {"findings": [], "gaps": []},
        analysis_results or {"findings": [], "gaps": []},
        query
    )

    result = json.loads(synthesis)

    # Step 4: Evaluate for gaps → re-delegate if coverage insufficient
    # THIS IS THE ITERATIVE REFINEMENT LOOP: evaluate → re-delegate → re-synthesize
    if result["coverage_gaps"]:
        print(f"\nStep 3: Coverage gaps detected: {result['coverage_gaps']}")
        print(f"  Re-delegating targeted search for gaps...")
        gap_search = search_subagent(f"{query} policy incentives")

        # Merge gap findings into existing results and RE-INVOKE synthesis
        merged_search = search_results or {"findings": [], "gaps": []}
        if gap_search:
            gap_data = gap_search  # Already a dict from search_subagent()
            merged_search["findings"].extend(gap_data.get("findings", []))
            merged_search["gaps"] = [g for g in merged_search["gaps"]
                                     if g not in [f["claim"] for f in gap_data.get("findings", [])]]

        print(f"  Re-invoking synthesis with {len(merged_search['findings'])} total findings...")
        refined_synthesis = synthesis_subagent(
            merged_search,
            analysis_results or {"findings": [], "gaps": []},
            query
        )
        result = json.loads(refined_synthesis)
        print(f"  Re-synthesis complete — gaps remaining: {result.get('coverage_gaps', [])}")
    else:
        print(f"\nStep 3: Coverage sufficient — no re-delegation needed")

    print(f"\nFINAL REPORT:")
    print(json.dumps(result, indent=2))
    return result


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Test 1: Full pipeline needed
    coordinator("What are the key trends in the EV market based on documents and research?")

    print("\n\n" + "="*60)

    # Test 2: Simple query — fewer subagents needed
    # The coordinator should NOT always route through the full pipeline
    coordinator("summarize the document's main points")

    Try It

    Ask Claude Code to create and run this file:

    Create the file lab-d1-agentic-arch/multi_agent.py with the code above and run it

    What you should see:

    • Coordinator analyzes the query and selects relevant subagents (not always all of them)
    • Each subagent returns findings with source attribution
    • Coordinator checks for coverage gaps and may re-delegate
    • Synthesis combines all findings into a unified response with citations

    Key observations:

    • Isolated context: synthesis_subagent receives ALL prior findings explicitly — it doesn't "remember" what search_subagent found
    • Dynamic selection: The coordinator decides which subagents to invoke based on the query
    • Gap detection: If synthesis finds gaps, coordinator re-delegates targeted queries
    • Attribution preserved: claim-source mappings flow through the pipeline intact

    Code Analysis

    Exercise 1 — What happens if you remove the synthesis step? If the coordinator returns raw subagent outputs without combining them, the user gets fragmented, overlapping findings with no unified narrative. The synthesis step is what creates a coherent report from isolated agent outputs.

    Exercise 2 — What happens if you don't pass prior findings to the synthesis subagent? Look at how synthesis_subagent() receives search_results and analysis_results as explicit parameters. If you omit these, the synthesis agent has no memory of what other agents found — it would re-research topics already covered instead of identifying what's missing. This is the core isolation principle.

    Exercise 3 — What happens if the coordinator delegates only ONE subtopic? This matches Sample Q7 on the exam. If the coordinator's task decomposition is too narrow (e.g., only researching "market size" but not "barriers" or "regional variation"), the final report has coverage gaps. The root cause is the coordinator's decomposition, not a subagent failure.

    Exam Essentials

    • If the exam says "report only covers X, missing Y and Z" → fix the coordinator's decomposition, NOT downstream agents
    • Wrong answer trap: "Improve the search agent's queries" — subagents did their job; they were assigned the wrong job
    • Wrong answer trap: "Add gap detection to synthesis" — synthesis can't synthesize what was never collected
    • The correct pattern: Broaden the coordinator's task decomposition to cover all relevant subtopics

    ✅ Lab 1.2 Checkpoint

    • Subagents have isolated context — prior findings must be passed explicitly
    • Coordinator decides dynamically which subagents to invoke
    • Synthesis receives all prior agent outputs in its prompt
    • Coverage gaps trigger targeted re-delegation → re-synthesis (iterative refinement loop)

    LAB 1.3: SUBAGENT CONTEXT PASSING AND SPAWNING

    Domain 1 — Task Statement 1.3 AgentDefinition, structured handoffs, parallel spawning ~20 minutesIntermediate | Requires: Claude Code

    Quick Recall (from previous labs)

    1. In hub-and-spoke, do subagents automatically inherit the coordinator's context? (Lab 1.2)
    2. What is the root cause when a research report only covers 2 of 5 subtopics? (Lab 1.2)

    Why This Matters

    The problem: Your coordinator delegates research to 3 subagents. They each return raw text blobs. When the synthesis agent combines them, it can't tell which claim came from which source. The final report says "revenue grew 14%" with no attribution — useless for verification.

    The fix: define a structured handoff format that every subagent must use. Each finding includes the claim, evidence, source, and date. Now the synthesis agent can merge findings AND preserve where each fact came from.

    Exam connection (Sample Q8): When a subagent fails, the coordinator needs structured error context (failure type, partial results, alternatives) — not just "error occurred." Same principle: structure enables intelligent downstream decisions.

    What You'll Learn

    • Structured handoff format: customer_id, root_cause, recommended_action — so downstream agents can act on findings without guessing
    • Parallel subagent spawning: The coordinator emits multiple Task calls in one response — subagents run concurrently, cutting latency
    • Goal-based vs step-by-step prompts: "Find the root cause" outperforms "Step 1: check logs, Step 2: check metrics" — Claude adapts better with goals
    • AgentDefinition: The SDK structure that configures each subagent (name, description, system_prompt, allowed_tools)

    See It In Action

    Open Claude Code and try this:

    I need you to do three things: (1) find all Python files in this directory, (2) count the total lines of code across them, and (3) summarize which files are the longest. Show me how you carried information from each step to the next.

    Watch how Claude Code passes context between steps. When it finds the files in step 1, it must carry that list forward to step 2. When it counts lines in step 2, it must carry those counts to step 3 for the summary. This is the structured handoff pattern — each phase's output becomes the next phase's input, and context doesn't transfer automatically.

    Reference Implementation: lab-d1-agentic-arch/context_passing.py

    import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

# ── STRUCTURED HANDOFF FORMAT ─────────────────────────────
# When passing context between agents, use structured formats
# that separate content from metadata (source, date, confidence).

def build_research_handoff(search_findings: list, analysis_findings: list) -> str:
    """
    Build a structured handoff for the synthesis subagent.

    Pattern: Content + Metadata (source URLs, doc names, page numbers)
    This preserves attribution through the synthesis step.
    """
    handoff = {
        "handoff_version": "1.0",
        "web_search_results": {
            "findings": search_findings,
            "metadata": {
                "search_timestamp": "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z",
                "queries_executed": len(search_findings),
                "coverage": "high"
            }
        },
        "document_analysis_results": {
            "findings": analysis_findings,
            "metadata": {
                "documents_analyzed": 3,
                "analysis_method": "section-by-section",
                "coverage": "medium"
            }
        }
    }
    return json.dumps(handoff, indent=2)


def demonstrate_parallel_spawning():
    """
    Demonstrates how a coordinator emits multiple Task calls
    in a single response to spawn parallel subagents.

    In Claude Agent SDK, a coordinator with tool_choice and Task tool
    can emit MULTIPLE Task tool calls in one response.
    These execute in parallel, not sequentially.
    """
    print("\n=== PARALLEL SPAWNING PATTERN ===")
    print("""
    In production (Agent SDK), the coordinator prompt would include:

    Tool: Task (the subagent spawning mechanism)
    allowedTools: ["Task"]  # coordinator MUST have Task in allowedTools

    A single coordinator response can contain MULTIPLE Task tool calls:

    Response content: [
        {"type": "tool_use", "name": "Task", "input": {
            "description": "Search for EV market trends",
            "prompt": "Search web for: EV market growth 2023-2024. Return structured findings."
        }},
        {"type": "tool_use", "name": "Task", "input": {
            "description": "Analyze regional report",
            "prompt": "Analyze this document for regional adoption patterns: [doc content]"
        }},
        {"type": "tool_use", "name": "Task", "input": {
            "description": "Search for battery technology",
            "prompt": "Search for: battery cost reduction trends 2023. Return structured findings."
        }}
    ]

    All three spawn simultaneously — true parallel execution.
    NOT: search → wait → analyze → wait → search2
    """)


def demonstrate_goal_based_prompt():
    """
    Shows goal-based vs step-by-step coordinator prompts.

    Goal-based prompts enable subagent adaptability.
    Step-by-step prompts make subagents rigid and brittle.
    """

    step_by_step = """
    STEP-BY-STEP (BAD — too rigid):
    1. First search for "EV market 2023"
    2. Then search for "EV battery costs"
    3. Then read the quarterly report
    4. Extract the three main statistics
    5. Write a 500-word summary
    """

    goal_based = """
    GOAL-BASED (GOOD — enables adaptability):
    Research the current state of the EV market.
    Quality criteria:
    - Cover market size, growth rate, and key barriers
    - Include at least 3 quantitative data points with sources
    - Identify regional variations if present
    - Note any conflicting statistics across sources
    Return structured findings with full source attribution.
    """

    print("\n=== GOAL-BASED VS STEP-BY-STEP PROMPTS ===")
    print(f"\nSTEP-BY-STEP (BAD):\n{step_by_step}")
    print(f"\nGOAL-BASED (GOOD):\n{goal_based}")
    print("""
    Why goal-based wins:
    - Subagent can adapt search queries based on what it finds
    - Not brittle when step 2 returns no results
    - Quality criteria let subagent self-evaluate coverage
    - Same prompt works for different topic domains
    """)


def demonstrate_context_in_synthesis_prompt():
    """
    Shows the exact structure of a synthesis subagent prompt
    that includes all prior context explicitly.
    """
    search_findings = [
        {"claim": "35% market growth", "source": "https://iea.org/2024", "date": "2024-01"},
        {"claim": "$139/kWh battery cost", "source": "https://bnef.com/2024", "date": "2024-02"},
    ]
    analysis_findings = [
        {"claim": "Regional adoption varies 3x", "source": "internal-report.pdf", "page": 12},
        {"claim": "Charging infrastructure top barrier", "source": "internal-report.pdf", "page": 18},
    ]

    structured_handoff = build_research_handoff(search_findings, analysis_findings)

    synthesis_prompt = f"""
You are a research synthesis specialist.

TASK: Synthesize the following research findings into a comprehensive report.
QUALITY CRITERIA:
- Preserve ALL source attributions from the input findings
- Flag any conflicting statistics with both sources cited
- Note coverage gaps explicitly

--- PRIOR AGENT FINDINGS (must be preserved in output) ---
{structured_handoff}
--- END PRIOR FINDINGS ---

Produce a structured synthesis report that a downstream report-generation
agent can use without needing to re-examine the original sources.
"""

    print("\n=== SYNTHESIS SUBAGENT PROMPT STRUCTURE ===")
    print("Synthesis prompt (first 600 chars):")
    print(synthesis_prompt[:600])
    print("\nKey pattern: ALL prior findings are in the prompt.")
    print("The synthesis agent has no other memory of what other agents found.")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    demonstrate_parallel_spawning()
    demonstrate_goal_based_prompt()
    demonstrate_context_in_synthesis_prompt()

    print("\n\n=== AGENTDEFINITION STRUCTURE ===")
    print("""
    In production (Agent SDK), each subagent is defined with:

    AgentDefinition(
        name="search_agent",
        description="Searches web for information on a given topic",
        system_prompt=\"\"\"You are a web search specialist.
        Return structured findings with source URLs and publication dates.
        Quality criteria: at least 3 sources, all claims cited.\"\"\",
        allowed_tools=["web_search", "fetch_url"],  # SCOPED — only search tools
        # NOT: all tools — scoped to role
    )

    AgentDefinition(
        name="synthesis_agent",
        description="Synthesizes findings from search and analysis agents",
        system_prompt=\"\"\"You are a research synthesis specialist.
        You will receive structured findings from prior agents.
        Preserve all source attributions in your output.\"\"\",
        allowed_tools=["verify_fact"],  # scoped cross-role tool for fact-checking
        # NOT: web_search — synthesis doesn't search independently
    )
    """)

    Create the file lab-d1-agentic-arch/context_passing.py with the code above and run it

    What you should see:

    • Structured handoff with source attribution fields (claim, source, date)
    • Parallel spawning output showing multiple subagents running concurrently
