    LAB 5.5: HUMAN REVIEW WORKFLOWS AND CONFIDENCE CALIBRATION

    Domain 5 — Task Statement 5.5 Stratified sampling, field-level confidence, accuracy by segment ~20 minutesAdvanced | Requires: Claude Code

    Quick Recall (from previous labs)

    1. What causes context degradation in extended sessions? (Lab 5.4)
    2. How do scratchpad files fix context degradation? (Lab 5.4)

    Why This Matters

    Your extraction pipeline reports 97% accuracy. You automate it. Then a client complains: handwritten invoices are extracted at 62% accuracy. The 97% aggregate masked the segment failure. The fix: validate accuracy by document type AND field before automating.

    Exam connection (Exercise 3): "Implement stratified random sampling of high-confidence extractions for ongoing error rate measurement."

    See It In Action

    Try this in Claude Code:

    > My extraction pipeline reports 97% accuracy overall. Here is the breakdown:
> - Digital PDF invoices (800 docs): 99% accuracy
> - Scanned paper invoices (150 docs): 91% accuracy
> - Handwritten invoices (50 docs): 62% accuracy
>
> My manager wants to automate all extractions since "97% is good enough."
> Why is this dangerous? What would happen to the handwritten invoices?
>
> Design a review routing system with these confidence thresholds:
> - Auto-approve: confidence >= 0.90
> - Spot-check: confidence 0.70-0.89
> - Human review: confidence < 0.70 OR ambiguous source
>
> Why must these thresholds be calibrated with labeled validation data
> rather than using the model's raw confidence scores?

    This demonstrates why aggregate accuracy masks segment failures and why confidence scores must be calibrated before trusting them for routing decisions.

    Reference Implementation: lab-d5-context-reliability/human_review.py

    import anthropic
import json
import random

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

# ── THE PROBLEM: AGGREGATE METRICS MASK SEGMENT FAILURES ──
# "97% overall accuracy" sounds great.
# But: 100% on simple invoices, 60% on handwritten invoices
# → Automating based on aggregate metric would cause 40% errors on handwritten docs

def demonstrate_segment_analysis():
    """Show why aggregate accuracy masks segment issues."""
    print("=== Aggregate vs Segment Accuracy ===\n")

    # Simulated accuracy data
    accuracy_data = [
        {"segment": "Digital PDF invoices",    "doc_count": 800, "accuracy": 0.99},
        {"segment": "Scanned paper invoices",  "doc_count": 150, "accuracy": 0.91},
        {"segment": "Handwritten invoices",    "doc_count": 50,  "accuracy": 0.62},
    ]

    total = sum(s["doc_count"] for s in accuracy_data)
    weighted_avg = sum(s["accuracy"] * s["doc_count"] for s in accuracy_data) / total

    print(f"Aggregate accuracy: {weighted_avg:.1%}  ← looks great!")
    print(f"\nBut by segment:")
    for s in accuracy_data:
        flag = " ← PROBLEM" if s["accuracy"] < 0.85 else ""
        print(f"  {s['segment']:35s}: {s['accuracy']:.0%}{flag}")

    print(f"\nConclusion: Automating 'high-confidence' extractions would fail")
    print(f"on {accuracy_data[2]['doc_count']} handwritten invoices at 62% accuracy.")
    print(f"Must validate accuracy by segment BEFORE reducing human review.")


def extraction_with_field_confidence(document: str) -> dict:
    """
    Extract data with field-level confidence scores.
    These scores must be CALIBRATED against labeled data — raw scores aren't reliable.
    """
    tool = {
        "name": "extract_with_confidence",
        "description": "Extract invoice data with per-field confidence scores",
        "input_schema": {
            "type": "object",
            "properties": {
                "vendor_name": {"type": "string"},
                "vendor_confidence": {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
                "total_amount": {"type": ["number", "null"]},
                "total_confidence": {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
                "invoice_date": {"type": ["string", "null"]},
                "date_confidence": {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
                "ambiguous_source": {"type": "boolean",
                                     "description": "True if source document has contradictions"}
            },
            "required": ["vendor_name", "vendor_confidence",
                         "total_confidence", "date_confidence", "ambiguous_source"]
        }
    }

    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-sonnet-4-6", max_tokens=512,
        tools=[tool],
        tool_choice={"type": "tool", "name": "extract_with_confidence"},
        messages=[{
            "role": "user",
            "content": (
                f"Extract invoice data with confidence scores.\n"
                f"Confidence 1.0 = completely certain, 0.0 = guessing.\n"
                f"Set ambiguous_source=true if the document has contradictions.\n\n"
                f"Document:\n{document}"
            )
        }]
    )

    for block in response.content:
        if block.type == "tool_use":
            return block.input
    return None


def route_for_review(extraction: dict, thresholds: dict) -> str:
    """
    Route based on calibrated confidence thresholds.

    Thresholds should be calibrated using labeled validation sets,
    not arbitrary numbers.
    """
    if extraction.get("ambiguous_source"):
        return "human_review"

    min_confidence = min(
        extraction.get("vendor_confidence", 0),
        extraction.get("total_confidence", 0),
        extraction.get("date_confidence", 0)
    )

    if min_confidence >= thresholds["auto_approve"]:
        return "auto_approve"
    elif min_confidence >= thresholds["spot_check"]:
        return "spot_check"
    else:
        return "human_review"


def stratified_sampling_demo(extractions: list, sample_rate: float = 0.05):
    """
    Stratified random sampling: sample high-confidence extractions
    to measure actual error rate and detect novel error patterns.
    """
    print("\n=== Stratified Sampling ===\n")

    high_confidence = [e for e in extractions if e.get("total_confidence", 0) >= 0.9]
    sample_size = max(1, int(len(high_confidence) * sample_rate))
    sample = random.sample(high_confidence, min(sample_size, len(high_confidence)))

    print(f"Total extractions:     {len(extractions)}")
    print(f"High-confidence (≥0.9): {len(high_confidence)}")
    print(f"Sample for review:     {len(sample)} ({sample_rate:.0%} of high-confidence)")
    print(f"\nPurpose: Verify 'high-confidence' claims are actually accurate.")
    print(f"If sample error rate > 5%: recalibrate thresholds")
    print(f"Watch for: novel error patterns not seen in training data")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    demonstrate_segment_analysis()

    print("\n\n=== Field-Level Confidence Extraction ===\n")
    test_docs = [
        "INVOICE #001\nVendor: Acme Corp\nDate: 2024-01-15\nTotal: $500.00",
        "inv from acme\ntotal somewhere around $500 or maybe $450\n date unclear",
        "INVOICE\nVendor: Widget Corp\nTotal: $300\nAlso total shows $350 on page 2",
    ]

    thresholds = {"auto_approve": 0.9, "spot_check": 0.7}

    for doc in test_docs:
        print(f"\nDoc: {doc[:60]}...")
        result = extraction_with_field_confidence(doc)
        if result:
            route = route_for_review(result, thresholds)
            print(f"  Confidences: vendor={result.get('vendor_confidence'):.2f} "
                  f"total={result.get('total_confidence'):.2f} "
                  f"date={result.get('date_confidence'):.2f}")
            print(f"  Ambiguous: {result.get('ambiguous_source')}")
            print(f"  → Route: {route}")

    # Simulate batch of extractions for sampling demo
    fake_extractions = [{"total_confidence": random.uniform(0.5, 1.0)} for _ in range(200)]
    stratified_sampling_demo(fake_extractions)

    print("\n\n=== Review Routing Architecture ===")
    print("""
    Routing pipeline:

    Extraction → Confidence scores → Route decision:
      ambiguous_source=true              → human_review (always)
      min_confidence ≥ 0.90              → auto_approve
      min_confidence 0.70-0.89           → spot_check (sample review)
      min_confidence < 0.70              → human_review

    Calibration process:
    1. Extract 500 labeled documents (known correct answers)
    2. Compare model confidence to actual accuracy at each confidence level
    3. Set thresholds where actual accuracy matches requirements
    4. Re-calibrate monthly as document types and accuracy evolve

    Ongoing monitoring:
    - Sample 5% of auto-approved extractions monthly
    - Measure error rate in sampled set
    - If error rate rises → lower auto-approve threshold → route more to review
    """)

    Try It

    Ask Claude Code to create and run this file:

    > Create the file lab-d5-context-reliability/human_review.py with the code above and run it.

    What you should see:

    • "Aggregate vs Segment Accuracy" showing 96.5% overall accuracy that masks a 62% accuracy problem on handwritten invoices (flagged as PROBLEM)
    • "Field-Level Confidence Extraction" processing 3 test invoices: a clean invoice (high confidence, auto-approved), a vague invoice (lower confidence, spot-check or human review), and a contradictory invoice (ambiguous_source=true, routed to human review)
    • "Stratified Sampling" showing how 5% of high-confidence extractions are sampled for human verification to catch novel error patterns
    • A "Review Routing Architecture" summary with the full routing pipeline and calibration process

    Code Analysis

    1. What happens if you trust the 97% aggregate accuracy and automate everything? (Answer: 38% error rate on handwritten invoices — clients get wrong data, you don't notice until complaints pile up. Aggregate metrics mask segment failures.)
    2. Why is stratified sampling of high-confidence extractions necessary? What if a new document format appears that the model hasn't seen? (Answer: novel error patterns go undetected without sampling. Stratified sampling catches accuracy drift before it becomes a crisis.)
    3. Why can't you trust raw model confidence scores for routing thresholds? (Answer: uncalibrated scores may be overconfident — a model reporting "90% confidence" may only be correct 70% of the time. Calibrate with labeled validation sets before trusting thresholds.)

    Exam Essentials

    • If the exam says "97% accuracy overall" → check accuracy BY SEGMENT, not just aggregate
    • Wrong answer trap: "Automate all high-confidence extractions" — aggregate masks poor segments
    • The correct pattern: Stratified sampling by document type and field. Validate each segment independently before automating.

    ✅ Lab 5.5 Checkpoint

    • Aggregate accuracy masks segment failures — validate by document type AND field
    • Field-level confidence scores must be calibrated with labeled validation sets
    • Stratified random sampling of high-confidence extractions detects novel error patterns
    • Route: ambiguous source → human; high confidence → auto; medium → spot-check
    • Ongoing monitoring: sample auto-approved items to detect accuracy drift

    LAB 5.6: INFORMATION PROVENANCE AND MULTI-SOURCE SYNTHESIS

    Domain 5 — Task Statement 5.6 Claim-source mappings, conflicting data, temporal metadata ~20 minutesAdvanced

    Quick Recall (from previous labs)

    1. Why can aggregate accuracy (e.g., "97% overall") be misleading? (Lab 5.5)
    2. What is stratified random sampling used for? (Lab 5.5)

    Why This Matters

    Your research synthesis says "the EV market grew 14%" without citing the source. A stakeholder asks "where did that number come from?" You can't answer — provenance was lost during summarization. The fix: require structured claim-source mappings from all subagents, preserved through synthesis.

    Exam connection: The exam tests claim-source mappings, conflicting data annotation (both values + sources, not picking one), and temporal metadata to prevent false contradictions.

    Reference Implementation: lab-d5-context-reliability/provenance.py

    import json
from datetime import datetime

# ── PROVENANCE THROUGH SYNTHESIS PIPELINE ────────────────
# Problem: summarization compresses findings without preserving claim-source mappings
# Solution: require structured claim-source format from all subagents

def demonstrate_provenance_loss():
    """Show how provenance is lost in naive summarization."""
    print("=== Provenance Loss in Naive Summarization ===\n")

    # Raw findings with provenance
    raw_findings = [
        {
            "claim": "Global EV market grew 35% in 2023",
            "source_url": "https://iea.org/reports/global-ev-outlook-2024",
            "source_name": "IEA Global EV Outlook 2024",
            "publication_date": "2024-01-15",
            "relevant_excerpt": "The global electric vehicle market saw 35% growth..."
        },
        {
            "claim": "Battery costs fell to $139/kWh",
            "source_url": "https://bnef.com/battery-price-survey-2024",
            "source_name": "BloombergNEF Battery Price Survey 2024",
            "publication_date": "2024-02-01",
            "relevant_excerpt": "Average battery pack prices reached $139/kWh..."
        }
    ]

    # BAD: Naive summarization loses provenance
    naive_summary = "The EV market grew 35% and battery costs fell to $139/kWh."
    print(f"Naive summary: '{naive_summary}'")
    print("Problem: No sources. Can't verify. Can't flag if sources conflict.")

    # GOOD: Structured claim-source mapping
    structured_summary = {
        "synthesis": "EV market grew 35% while battery costs declined to $139/kWh",
        "claims": [
            {
                "claim": raw_findings[0]["claim"],
                "source": raw_findings[0]["source_name"],
                "source_url": raw_findings[0]["source_url"],
                "publication_date": raw_findings[0]["publication_date"],
                "excerpt": raw_findings[0]["relevant_excerpt"]
            },
            {
                "claim": raw_findings[1]["claim"],
                "source": raw_findings[1]["source_name"],
                "source_url": raw_findings[1]["source_url"],
                "publication_date": raw_findings[1]["publication_date"],
                "excerpt": raw_findings[1]["relevant_excerpt"]
            }
        ]
    }

    print(f"\nStructured summary:\n{json.dumps(structured_summary, indent=2)}")
    print("\nProvenance preserved through synthesis step.")


def demonstrate_conflicting_sources():
    """Show how to handle conflicting statistics from credible sources."""
    print("\n=== Handling Conflicting Statistics ===\n")

    conflicting_data = [
        {
            "claim": "EV market share reached 18% globally in 2023",
            "source": "IEA Global EV Outlook 2024",
            "publication_date": "2024-01-15",
            "methodology": "Includes all BEV and PHEV vehicles"
        },
        {
            "claim": "EV market share was 14% globally in 2023",
            "source": "BloombergNEF EV Forecast 2024",
            "publication_date": "2024-02-01",
            "methodology": "Battery electric vehicles only (excludes PHEV)"
        }
    ]

    print("Two credible sources, different numbers:\n")
    for d in conflicting_data:
        print(f"  {d['source']}: {d['claim']}")
        print(f"  Methodology: {d['methodology']}\n")

    # BAD: Pick one arbitrarily
    bad_synthesis = "EV market share was 18% globally in 2023."
    print(f"BAD synthesis (picks one): '{bad_synthesis}'")
    print("Problem: Discards valid data. May mislead reader.\n")

    # GOOD: Annotate conflict with both sources
    good_synthesis = {
        "topic": "Global EV market share 2023",
        "synthesized_finding": "EV market share ranged from 14-18% depending on methodology",
        "conflict_detected": True,
        "source_comparison": [
            {
                "claim": d["claim"],
                "source": d["source"],
                "source_url": f"https://example.com/{d['source'].lower().replace(' ', '-')}",
                "publication_date": d["publication_date"],
                "methodology_note": d["methodology"]
            }
            for d in conflicting_data
        ],
        "resolution_note": (
            "The difference (14% vs 18%) is explained by methodology: "
            "IEA includes PHEVs while BNEF counts BEVs only. "
            "Both figures are correct for their respective definitions."
        )
    }

    print(f"GOOD synthesis (annotates conflict):\n{json.dumps(good_synthesis, indent=2)}")


def demonstrate_temporal_metadata():
    """Show why publication dates prevent false contradictions."""
    print("\n\n=== Temporal Metadata ===\n")

    findings_without_dates = [
        "Battery costs were $400/kWh",
        "Battery costs fell to $139/kWh"
    ]

    print("Without dates, these look contradictory:")
    for f in findings_without_dates:
        print(f"  '{f}'")
    print("Problem: Is one wrong? Or are they from different years?\n")

    findings_with_dates = [
        {"claim": "Battery costs were $400/kWh", "publication_date": "2015-01-01",
         "source": "BNEF 2015 Survey"},
        {"claim": "Battery costs fell to $139/kWh", "publication_date": "2024-02-01",
         "source": "BNEF 2024 Survey"}
    ]

    print("With dates, the 'contradiction' is resolved:")
    for f in findings_with_dates:
        print(f"  [{f['publication_date']}] '{f['claim']}' — {f['source']}")
    print("\nConclusion: Battery costs dropped 65% over 9 years. No contradiction.")

    print("""
    Required temporal metadata in subagent outputs:
    - publication_date: when the source was published
    - data_collection_date: when the underlying data was collected (may differ from pub date)
    - as_of_date: what time period the statistic represents

    Without this: old statistics look like contradictions to recent ones.
    With this: temporal differences are visible and interpretable.
    """)


def build_synthesis_subagent_prompt(search_results: list, analysis_results: list) -> str:
    """
    Builds synthesis prompt that REQUIRES claim-source preservation.
    """
    return f"""
Synthesize the following research findings into a comprehensive report.

CRITICAL REQUIREMENTS:
1. Preserve ALL source attributions — every claim must have its source URL and publication date
2. When two sources conflict: annotate with BOTH sources, explain the likely reason
3. Include temporal metadata (publication_date) in all structured claim outputs
4. Do NOT summarize away specific numbers, dates, or source references

Search agent findings:
{json.dumps(search_results, indent=2)}

Analysis agent findings:
{json.dumps(analysis_results, indent=2)}

Output format:
{{
  "synthesis_text": "...",
  "claims": [
    {{
      "claim": "...",
      "source": "...",
      "source_url": "...",
      "publication_date": "...",
      "excerpt": "..."
    }}
  ],
  "conflicts": [
    {{
      "topic": "...",
      "sources": [...],
      "resolution_note": "..."
    }}
  ]
}}
"""


if __name__ == "__main__":
    demonstrate_provenance_loss()
    demonstrate_conflicting_sources()
    demonstrate_temporal_metadata()

    print("\n\n=== Subagent Output Requirements for Provenance ===")
    prompt = build_synthesis_subagent_prompt(
        search_results=[{"claim": "test", "source_url": "https://example.com",
                          "publication_date": "2024-01"}],
        analysis_results=[{"claim": "test2", "source": "doc.pdf", "page": 5}]
    )
    print("Synthesis prompt structure (first 400 chars):")
    print(prompt[:400])

    print("\n\n=== Key Exam Concept ===")
    print("""
    Provenance is lost at summarization steps unless you require its preservation.

    Require from ALL subagents:
    - source_url (not just source name)
    - publication_date
    - relevant_excerpt (not just the claim)

    Handle conflicts by:
    - Annotating with BOTH sources (not picking one)
    - Explaining the methodology difference
    - Including temporal context

    The synthesis agent's job is to COMBINE findings, not COMPRESS them.
    """)

    Try It

    Ask Claude Code to create and run this file:

    Create lab-d5-context-reliability/provenance.py with the code above and run it

    What you should see:

    • "Provenance Loss in Naive Summarization" showing a bare summary with no sources vs a structured claim-source mapping with source_url, publication_date, and excerpt for each claim
    • "Handling Conflicting Statistics" showing two credible sources reporting different EV market share numbers (14% vs 18%), with the BAD synthesis picking one arbitrarily vs the GOOD synthesis annotating both with methodology differences
    • "Temporal Metadata" demonstrating how two battery cost claims ($400/kWh vs $139/kWh) look contradictory without dates but are resolved as a 9-year trend when publication dates are included
    • A synthesis prompt structure requiring claim-source preservation and conflict annotation in the output format

    Reference: Multi-content-type rendering in synthesis

    Different content types need different formatting. The exam tests this specifically: "Render financial data as tables, news as prose, technical findings as structured lists." Converting everything to one format loses meaning.

    def demonstrate_content_type_rendering():
    """
    Synthesis output should render each content type in its natural format.
    Not: convert everything to prose (loses table structure)
    Not: convert everything to bullets (loses narrative flow)
    """

    # Example synthesis output with type-appropriate rendering
    synthesis_output = """
## Research Synthesis: EV Market Analysis

### Market Overview
[NEWS — render as prose]
Global EV adoption accelerated in 2023, driven primarily by policy incentives in
Europe and falling battery costs in Asian markets. Consumer sentiment shifted
markedly toward EVs in Q3, coinciding with new model launches from major OEMs.

### Financial Data
[FINANCIAL — render as table]

| Metric                | 2022     | 2023     | Change  |
|-----------------------|----------|----------|---------|
| Market size (units)   | 10.5M    | 14.2M    | +35%    |
| Battery cost ($/kWh)  | $161     | $139     | -14%    |
| Average EV price      | $54,000  | $47,200  | -13%    |
| Market share (global) | 13%      | 18%      | +5pp    |

### Technical Findings
[TECHNICAL — render as structured list]

Battery Technology:
- Lithium iron phosphate (LFP) chemistry gaining market share due to lower cost
- Solid-state batteries: 2027-2028 commercial availability (Toyota, Samsung SDI)
- Fast charging: 350kW peak now standard in new premium models

Charging Infrastructure:
- DC fast charger installations: +67% YoY in North America
- Grid integration: V2G pilots in 8 countries, commercial deployment 2025-2026

### Source Attribution
All findings include original claim-source mappings. See appendix for full citations.
"""

    print(synthesis_output)

    print("""
    Why type-appropriate rendering matters:

    Financial data as prose:
    → "Revenue was $54,000 in 2022 and fell to $47,200 in 2023, a 13% decrease"
    ✗ Hard to compare multiple metrics | Can't see trends at a glance

    News as bullet points:
    → "• Global EV adoption accelerated | • Policy incentives drove growth | • Sentiment shifted"
    ✗ Loses narrative causality | "driven by" and "coinciding with" relationships disappear

    Technical findings as paragraph:
    → "LFP is gaining share. Solid state will be ready 2027-2028. Toyota and Samsung..."
    ✗ Hard to scan | Important items buried in prose

    EXAM RULE: The synthesis agent should specify content type in structured output
    so the report generator renders each section correctly.
    """)

    # How to instruct synthesis agent
    synthesis_instruction = """
Your synthesis report must specify the appropriate format for each section:

Financial data:
- ALWAYS render as markdown tables
- Include: metric name, values per period, delta/trend

News/market developments:
- Render as flowing prose paragraphs
- Preserve causal relationships ("driven by", "following", "coinciding with")

Technical specifications:
- Render as nested bullet lists
- Group by category (battery, charging, software)

Do NOT convert all content to a single uniform format.
"""
    print("Synthesis instruction snippet:")
    print(synthesis_instruction)

demonstrate_content_type_rendering()

    Code Analysis

    1. What happens if source attribution is removed from subagent outputs? The synthesis agent can't cite sources — "14% growth" appears with no source, making the report unverifiable. Provenance must be preserved through the entire pipeline.
    2. When two sources conflict, should the synthesis agent pick one? No — annotate BOTH values with their sources and methodology, and let the reader decide. Arbitrarily dropping data is an anti-pattern.
    3. Two sources report different CEO names. Is this a conflict? Maybe not — the CEO may have changed. Temporal metadata (publication dates) prevents false contradictions.

    Exam Essentials

    • If the exam says "report cites statistics without sources" → claim-source mappings lost during synthesis
    • Wrong answer trap: "Give synthesis agent access to original sources" — re-verification is expensive and misses the root cause
    • The correct pattern: Require structured claim-source mappings from subagents, preserved through synthesis

    ✅ Lab 5.6 Checkpoint

    • Provenance is lost at summarization unless explicitly required to be preserved
    • Require: source_url, publication_date, relevant_excerpt from all subagents
    • Conflicting statistics: annotate with both sources + methodology difference
    • Temporal metadata prevents false contradictions (different years look like conflicts)
    • Synthesis = combine findings, not compress them
    • Render by content type: financial → tables, news → prose, technical → structured lists
    • Converting everything to one format loses meaning inherent to that content type

    Quick Check — Module 5

    Q: After a 15-turn support conversation, your agent says "your order was approximately $150" when the actual total from turn 3 was $149.99. What pattern prevents this?

    A) Increase the context window B) Extract transactional facts into a persistent case facts block C) Use progressive summarization D) Have the agent re-read all prior tool results

    Answer

    B. Case facts blocks persist exact values outside summarized history. Progressive summarization (C) is actually the CAUSE — it compresses "$149.99" into "approximately $150." (Lab 5.1)

    Q: Your agent escalates 45% of cases (target: 20%). It escalates simple damage replacements but tries to handle policy exceptions. What's the best fix?

    A) Add explicit escalation criteria with few-shot examples B) Add sentiment analysis C) Have the agent self-report confidence scores D) Deploy a trained classifier

    Answer

    A. Explicit criteria with examples fix unclear decision boundaries. Sentiment (B) doesn't correlate with complexity. Self-confidence (C) is poorly calibrated. A classifier (D) is over-engineered before trying prompt optimization. (Lab 5.2, Exam Sample Q3)

    import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()


# DOMAIN 1: Data layer (fake backend)


CUSTOMERS = {
    "jane@email.com": {"id": "CUST-001", "name": "Jane Smith", "tier": "gold",
                       "email": "jane@email.com", "phone": "555-0101",
                       "created_at": 1704067200,  # Unix timestamp (will be normalized)
                       "status": 1},               # Numeric status (will be normalized)
    "bob@email.com":  {"id": "CUST-002", "name": "Bob Jones", "tier": "silver",
                       "email": "bob@email.com",  "phone": "555-0102",
                       "created_at": 1706745600,
                       "status": 1}
}

ORDERS = {
    "ORD-555": {"id": "ORD-555", "customer_id": "CUST-001",
                "items": ["Blue Widget x2", "Red Gadget x1"],
                "total": 149.99, "status": "shipped",
                "tracking": "1Z999AA10123456784",
                "delivery_eta": "2024-01-18",
                "warehouse_id": "WH-007", "picker_id": "EMP-1234",  # irrelevant fields
                "insurance_value": 149.99, "weight_lbs": 2.3},       # irrelevant fields
    "ORD-777": {"id": "ORD-777", "customer_id": "CUST-002",
                "items": ["Green Thing x1"], "total": 29.99,
                "status": "processing", "tracking": None,
                "delivery_eta": None,
                "warehouse_id": "WH-003", "picker_id": None}
}


# DOMAIN 1: PostToolUse Hook — Data Normalization


STATUS_MAP = {1: "active", 2: "suspended", 3: "closed"}

from datetime import datetime

def post_tool_use_normalize(tool_name: str, result: dict) -> dict:
    """Normalize data formats before model sees results."""
    if "created_at" in result and isinstance(result["created_at"], int):
        result["created_at"] = datetime.fromtimestamp(result["created_at"]).isoformat()
    if "status" in result and isinstance(result["status"], int):
        result["status"] = STATUS_MAP.get(result["status"], "unknown")
    return result


# DOMAIN 5: Tool Result Trimming


CUSTOMER_RELEVANT_FIELDS = {"id", "name", "email", "tier", "status"}
ORDER_RELEVANT_FIELDS     = {"id", "status", "total", "items", "tracking", "delivery_eta"}

def trim_customer(c: dict) -> dict:
    return {k: v for k, v in c.items() if k in CUSTOMER_RELEVANT_FIELDS}

def trim_order(o: dict) -> dict:
    return {k: v for k, v in o.items() if k in ORDER_RELEVANT_FIELDS}


# DOMAIN 1: Prerequisite Gate State


verified_customer_id = None
case_facts = {}  # Domain 5: persistent case facts


# DOMAIN 2: Tool Execution with Structured Errors


def execute_tool(name, input_data):
    global verified_customer_id, case_facts

    if name == "get_customer":
        email = input_data.get("email", "")

        if not email or "@" not in email:
            return json.dumps({
                "isError": True, "errorCategory": "validation",
                "isRetryable": False,
                "message": f"Invalid email format: '{email}'"
            })

        c = CUSTOMERS.get(email)
        if c:
            # Domain 1: PostToolUse hook — normalize data
            c = post_tool_use_normalize("get_customer", dict(c))
            # Domain 5: Trim to relevant fields
            c_trimmed = trim_customer(c)
            verified_customer_id = c_trimmed["id"]
            print(f"    ✓ Customer verified: {verified_customer_id}")
            # Domain 5: Update case facts
            case_facts.update({"customer_id": verified_customer_id,
                                "email": email, "tier": c_trimmed["tier"]})
            return json.dumps(c_trimmed)

        return json.dumps({
            "isError": False, "results": None,
            "message": f"No customer found with email '{email}'."
        })

    elif name == "lookup_order":
        # Domain 1: Prerequisite gate
        if verified_customer_id is None:
            return json.dumps({
                "isError": True, "errorCategory": "validation",
                "isRetryable": False,
                "message": "Customer verification required. Call get_customer first."
            })
        order_id = input_data.get("order_id", "")
        o = ORDERS.get(order_id)
        if o:
            # Domain 5: Trim to relevant fields
            o_trimmed = trim_order(dict(o))
            case_facts.setdefault("order_ids", [])
            if order_id not in case_facts["order_ids"]:
                case_facts["order_ids"].append(order_id)
            return json.dumps(o_trimmed)
        return json.dumps({
            "isError": False, "results": None,
            "message": f"No order found with ID '{order_id}'."
        })

    elif name == "process_refund":
        # Domain 1: Prerequisite gate
        if verified_customer_id is None:
            return json.dumps({
                "isError": True, "errorCategory": "validation",
                "isRetryable": False,
                "message": "Customer verification required. Call get_customer first."
            })
        amount = input_data.get("amount", 0)
        order_id = input_data.get("order_id", "unknown")

        # Domain 1: Policy gate (PreToolUse hook pattern)
        if amount > 500:
            print(f"    ✗ BLOCKED: ${amount} > $500 policy limit")
            return json.dumps({
                "isError": True, "errorCategory": "business",
                "isRetryable": False,
                "message": f"Refund of ${amount} exceeds $500 auto-approval limit.",
                "customer_friendly_message": "This refund requires manager approval. You'll be contacted within 24 hours.",
                "redirect": "escalate_to_human"
            })

        print(f"    ✓ Refund processed: ${amount} for {order_id}")
        case_facts.setdefault("refund_amounts", [])
        case_facts["refund_amounts"].append(amount)
        return json.dumps({"success": True, "refund_amount": amount,
                           "order_id": order_id, "customer_id": verified_customer_id})

    elif name == "escalate_to_human":
        summary = input_data.get("summary", "")
        reason  = input_data.get("reason", "unspecified")
        print(f"\n    → ESCALATING: reason={reason}")
        print(f"      Customer: {input_data.get('customer_id', verified_customer_id)}")
        print(f"      Summary: {summary[:120]}")
        return json.dumps({"escalated": True, "ticket_id": "TKT-9999",
                           "assigned_agent": "Sarah (Senior Support)"})

    return json.dumps({"error": f"Unknown tool: {name}"})



# DOMAIN 2: Tool Definitions (well-described)


tools = [
    {
        "name": "get_customer",
        "description": (
            "Retrieves customer profile by email address. "
            "Input: email (string). "
            "Returns: customer ID, name, membership tier, account status. "
            "ALWAYS call this first before any order lookup or refund operations. "
            "Do NOT use for: looking up order details, tracking numbers."
        ),
        "input_schema": {"type": "object",
                         "properties": {"email": {"type": "string",
                                                  "description": "Customer's email address"}},
                         "required": ["email"]}
    },
    {
        "name": "lookup_order",
        "description": (
            "Retrieves order details by order ID (format: 'ORD-NNN'). "
            "Returns: status, items, total, tracking number, delivery ETA. "
            "Requires: get_customer must be called first. "
            "Use when: customer mentions a specific order ID or asks about order status/tracking."
        ),
        "input_schema": {"type": "object",
                         "properties": {"order_id": {"type": "string",
                                                     "description": "Order ID, e.g. ORD-555"}},
                         "required": ["order_id"]}
    },
    {
        "name": "process_refund",
        "description": (
            "Issues a refund for a customer's order. "
            "Input: order_id, amount (numeric, no currency symbol). "
            "Requires: get_customer must succeed first. "
            "Limit: refunds over $500 automatically escalate to human agent. "
            "Use for: damaged items, missing items, incorrect orders, standard returns."
        ),
        "input_schema": {"type": "object",
                         "properties": {"order_id": {"type": "string"},
                                        "amount":   {"type": "number",
                                                     "description": "Refund amount in dollars"}},
                         "required": ["order_id", "amount"]}
    },
    {
        "name": "escalate_to_human",
        "description": (
            "Transfers case to a human agent. "
            "Use ONLY when: (1) customer explicitly requests human, "
            "(2) policy gap exists, (3) no progress after full investigation, "
            "(4) refund over $500. "
            "Do NOT use for: frustrated customers whose issue you can resolve, "
            "standard returns/refunds within policy."
        ),
        "input_schema": {
            "type": "object",
            "properties": {
                "reason": {"type": "string",
                           "enum": ["explicit_customer_request", "policy_gap",
                                    "no_progress", "high_value_refund"]},
                "customer_id": {"type": ["string", "null"]},
                "summary":  {"type": "string",
                             "description": "Brief summary of the issue"},
                "root_cause": {"type": "string"},
                "recommended_action": {"type": "string"}
            },
            "required": ["reason", "summary", "root_cause", "recommended_action"]
        }
    }
]


# DOMAINS 4+5: System prompt with explicit criteria, few-shot escalation


SYSTEM_PROMPT = """You are a customer support agent.
Resolve issues autonomously when possible. Aim for first-contact resolution.

ESCALATION CRITERIA — EXAMPLES:
Escalate IMMEDIATELY (no investigation):
  "I want to speak to a manager" → escalate_to_human(reason="explicit_customer_request")
  "Let me talk to a real person" → escalate_to_human(reason="explicit_customer_request")

Escalate for POLICY GAP:
  Customer asks for competitor price match → policy only covers own-site → escalate
  Refund > $500 → process_refund will redirect automatically

Escalate for NO PROGRESS:
  Same issue after full investigation → escalate_to_human(reason="no_progress")

DO NOT ESCALATE — handle autonomously:
  Standard return within 30 days → look up order → process refund
  Frustrated customer, issue within capability:
    → Acknowledge frustration, offer resolution
    → Escalate ONLY if they repeat the human request

CONTEXT: Always verify customer identity FIRST with get_customer.
"""


# The Agent Loop


def run_support_agent(user_message: str):
    global verified_customer_id, case_facts
    verified_customer_id = None
    case_facts = {}

    print(f"\n{'='*65}")
    print(f"CUSTOMER: {user_message}")
    print(f"{'='*65}\n")

    messages = [{"role": "user", "content": user_message}]
    iteration = 0

    while True:
        iteration += 1
        print(f"  [Loop iteration {iteration}]")

        # Domain 5: Include case facts block in system context if populated
        system = SYSTEM_PROMPT
        if case_facts:
            facts_block = "\n\n--- CASE FACTS (verified, persist across turns) ---\n"
            for key, val in case_facts.items():
                facts_block += f"  {key}: {val}\n"
            facts_block += "--- END CASE FACTS ---"
            system = SYSTEM_PROMPT + facts_block

        response = client.messages.create(
            model="claude-sonnet-4-6",
            max_tokens=1024,
            system=system,
            tools=tools,
            messages=messages
        )

        print(f"  stop_reason: {response.stop_reason}")

        if response.stop_reason == "end_turn":
            text = "".join(b.text for b in response.content if hasattr(b, "text"))
            print(f"\nAGENT RESPONSE:\n{text}\n")
            if case_facts:
                print(f"Case facts accumulated: {json.dumps(case_facts)}")
            return text

        elif response.stop_reason == "tool_use":
            messages.append({"role": "assistant", "content": response.content})
            results = []
            for b in response.content:
                if b.type == "tool_use":
                    print(f"  Tool: {b.name}({json.dumps(b.input)[:60]})")
                    results.append({
                        "type": "tool_result",
                        "tool_use_id": b.id,
                        "content": execute_tool(b.name, b.input)
                    })
            messages.append({"role": "user", "content": results})
        else:
            break



# Test Scenarios (maps to all 6 exam scenarios)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    print("\n=== Scenario 1: Standard refund (Domains 1, 2) ===")
    run_support_agent("I'm jane@email.com. My order ORD-555 arrived damaged. I want a refund.")

    print("\n=== Scenario 2: Over-limit refund (Domain 1 gate) ===")
    run_support_agent("I'm jane@email.com. I need a $750 refund for ORD-555.")

    print("\n=== Scenario 3: Explicit human request (Domain 5 escalation) ===")
    run_support_agent("I want to speak to a manager right now. This is unacceptable.")

    print("\n=== Scenario 4: Policy gap (Domain 5 escalation) ===")
    run_support_agent("I'm jane@email.com. I found the same item at Amazon for $50 less. Will you price match?")

    print("\n=== Scenario 5: Frustrated but resolvable (Domain 5 nuance) ===")
    run_support_agent("I'm bob@email.com. I'm really frustrated, my order ORD-777 still says processing.")

    Try It

    Ask Claude Code to create and run this file:

    > Create the file lab-final-scenario/complete_agent.py with the code above and run it.

    What you should see:

    • Five scenarios running sequentially, each showing loop iterations with stop_reason and tool calls printed at each step
    • Scenario 1 (standard refund): get_customer -> lookup_order -> process_refund -> end_turn, with "Customer verified" and "Refund processed" confirmations and accumulated case facts printed at the end
    • Scenario 2 (over-limit refund): process_refund BLOCKED at $750 (exceeds $500 policy limit), automatically escalated to human agent with a ticket ID
    • Scenario 3 (explicit human request): immediate escalation with no tool investigation, honoring the customer's request to speak to a manager

    What to observe in each scenario

    1. Standard refund: get_customer → lookup_order → process_refund → end_turn Gate enforced (customer verified before refund), trimmed tool results

    2. Over-limit: get_customer → lookup_order → process_refund (BLOCKED) → escalate_to_human Policy gate fires, structured escalation handoff with all required fields

    3. Explicit request: escalate_to_human immediately No investigation — explicit requests honored without "let me try first"

    4. Policy gap: get_customer → escalate_to_human(reason="policy_gap") Agent correctly identifies competitor pricing as outside current policy

    5. Frustrated but resolvable: get_customer → lookup_order → response Acknowledges frustration, offers to help, does NOT immediately escalate

    Code Analysis

    Study the complete agent implementation and answer these questions about each domain:

    1. Domain 1 (gates): What happens if you remove the prerequisite gate? Can process_refund be called without customer verification? (Answer: yes — this is Sample Q1's exact failure mode. Prompt-only enforcement fails at a non-zero rate.)
    2. Domain 1 (hooks): What role does the PostToolUse hook play? What happens with mixed date formats without normalization? (Answer: inconsistent comparisons — normalization ensures the model always sees dates in ISO format.)
    3. Domain 5 (context): Why is the case facts block injected into the system prompt on every iteration? (Answer: it preserves exact values like $149.99 that progressive summarization would compress to "approximately $150".)
    4. Domain 4+5 (escalation): What makes the escalation criteria in the system prompt reliable? Why not use sentiment analysis? (Answer: explicit categorical triggers — "customer requests human," "policy gap" — are binary and verifiable. Sentiment doesn't correlate with case complexity.)
    5. Domain 2 (tools): Why does each tool description include "when to use" AND "when NOT to use"? (Answer: disambiguation. Without negative examples, similar tools get confused — the model needs to know the boundaries of each tool's purpose.)

    Exam Essentials

    • This lab combines ALL domains. On the exam, each scenario question can test ANY domain.
    • The universal rule: Deterministic compliance = programmatic (gates, hooks, schema). Probabilistic guidance = prompts (few-shot, criteria).
    • The universal trap: Using prompts for compliance requirements, or using programmatic enforcement for stylistic preferences.

    EXAM READINESS CHECKLIST

    After completing all labs, verify you understand these. Each item maps to an exam-tested concept.

    Domain 1: Agentic Architecture (27%)

    • UNDERSTAND the agentic loop — stop_reason controls every iteration, not text parsing
    • KNOW why removing tool result appending breaks the loop (Code Analysis, Lab 1.1)
    • UNDERSTAND the text-parsing anti-pattern and why it fails
    • UNDERSTAND multi-agent coordinator with explicit context passing between subagents
    • KNOW that subagents have isolated context (must receive findings explicitly)
    • UNDERSTAND the iterative refinement loop: evaluate gaps → re-delegate → re-synthesize
    • KNOW parallel subagent spawning = multiple Task calls in one response
    • UNDERSTAND fork_session for exploring divergent approaches from shared baseline
    • UNDERSTAND programmatic prerequisite gates and why prompt-only is unreliable
    • KNOW multi-concern decomposition: N issues → investigate each → unified response
    • UNDERSTAND PostToolUse normalization and PreToolUse blocking hooks
    • CAN CHOOSE prompt chaining vs dynamic decomposition for a given use case
    • CAN CHOOSE --resume vs fork_session vs fresh start (decision framework, Lab 1.7)
    • UNDERSTAND high-impact area identification for open-ended task decomposition (Lab 1.6)

    Domain 2: Tool Design & MCP (18%)

    • UNDERSTAND why good tool descriptions are the #1 fix for tool selection issues
    • KNOW how to split a generic tool into purpose-specific tools with defined contracts
    • UNDERSTAND keyword-sensitive system prompt impact on tool associations
    • KNOW all 4 error categories: transient, validation, business, permission
    • UNDERSTAND subagent local error recovery (retry transient → propagate non-retryable)
    • KNOW the difference between access failure and valid empty result
    • UNDERSTAND constrained tool replacement (fetch_url → load_document)
    • KNOW tool_choice auto, any, and forced — and when to use each
    • UNDERSTAND .mcp.json (project) vs ~/.claude.json (user) scoping
    • KNOW MCP resources vs tools — resources for content catalogs, tools for actions
    • KNOW when to use community MCP servers (standard integrations) vs custom
    • CAN SELECT the right built-in tool: Grep/Glob for search, Read/Write/Edit for files

    Domain 3: Claude Code Configuration (20%)

    • UNDERSTAND the full CLAUDE.md hierarchy (user, project, directory levels)
    • KNOW @import syntax for modularizing CLAUDE.md
    • UNDERSTAND path-specific rules with YAML frontmatter paths: glob patterns
    • KNOW project slash commands and skills with frontmatter (context:fork, allowed-tools)
    • UNDERSTAND context:fork isolates skill output from main conversation
    • KNOW the Explore subagent isolates verbose discovery output
    • CAN COMBINE plan mode (investigation) → direct execution (implementation)
    • CAN DECIDE correctly: plan mode vs direct execution for given scenarios
    • KNOW /memory verifies loaded config and diagnoses inconsistencies
    • KNOW -p flag is required for non-interactive CI mode
    • KNOW --output-format json AND --json-schema for schema-enforced CI output
    • UNDERSTAND why existing test files in context prevent duplicate suggestions
    • UNDERSTAND why independent review instances beat self-review

    Domain 4: Prompt Engineering (20%)

    • UNDERSTAND specific categorical criteria vs vague "be conservative"
    • KNOW the interim trust restoration pattern: disable high-FP category → fix → re-enable
    • KNOW how to create 2-4 few-shot examples with ambiguous case handling
    • UNDERSTAND structured extraction with tool_use and nullable fields
    • KNOW tool_choice "any" with multiple schemas — model picks the right extraction
    • UNDERSTAND retry loops with specific error feedback (not vague "try again")
    • KNOW detected_pattern field for analyzing dismissal rates and false positive sources
    • KNOW the three validation layers: JSON Schema (syntax) → Pydantic (types) → Custom (semantics)
    • CAN DECIDE batch API vs synchronous: 50% savings, 24hr window, non-blocking only
    • UNDERSTAND multi-instance review: independent reviewer beats self-review
    • KNOW multi-pass: per-file local + cross-file integration prevents attention dilution
    • UNDERSTAND confidence-based routing: auto (0.9+), spot-check (0.7-0.9), human (<0.7)

    Domain 5: Context Management (15%)

    • UNDERSTAND case facts blocks that persist exact values across conversation turns
    • UNDERSTAND tool result trimming (keep only relevant fields)
    • KNOW "lost in the middle" effect and the summary-first mitigation
    • UNDERSTAND explicit escalation criteria with few-shot examples
    • KNOW: explicit human request → immediate escalation (no investigation)
    • KNOW: policy gap → escalate; complex but within policy → resolve (Lab 5.2)
    • KNOW: multiple customer matches → ask for identifiers, not heuristic selection
    • UNDERSTAND structured error context from subagents (not generic error strings)
    • KNOW scratchpad files for extended exploration sessions
    • UNDERSTAND subagent delegation: verbose exploration in isolated context, summary returned
    • UNDERSTAND stratified sampling for human review workflows
    • KNOW claim-source mappings must be preserved through synthesis pipeline
    • KNOW content type rendering: financial → tables, news → prose, technical → structured lists

    How to Use This for Final Exam Prep

    1. Complete every lab — study the reference code, run it via Claude Code, and answer the Code Analysis questions. The exam tests judgment from experience.

    2. Trace through the Code Analysis exercises — understand what breaks when you remove a gate, use the wrong termination signal, or suppress errors. The exam tests your understanding of WHY patterns fail.

    3. Know the exam scenarios cold:

      • Scenario 1: Customer Support → Domains 1, 2, 5
      • Scenario 2: Claude Code → Domains 3, 5
      • Scenario 3: Multi-Agent Research → Domains 1, 2, 5
      • Scenario 4: Developer Productivity → Domains 2, 3, 1
      • Scenario 5: CI/CD Pipeline → Domains 3, 4
      • Scenario 6: Structured Extraction → Domains 4, 5

    4. The exam pattern: Every question has one clearly correct answer and three plausible wrong ones. The wrong ones are usually:

      • "Use prompts" when programmatic is required
      • "Self-review" when independent instance is correct
      • "Generic error message" when structured error is needed
      • "Resume session" when starting fresh with injected summary is better

    5. The core exam thesis: Deterministic guarantees require programmatic solutions. Probabilistic guidance uses prompts. Know which situation requires which approach.

    PRACTICE QUESTIONS — SELF-TEST

    These follow the exact format of the real exam: one correct answer, three plausible distractors. After completing all labs, you should be able to answer every one correctly.

    Domain 1 Practice Questions

    Q1 (Task 1.1). Your agentic loop occasionally exits mid-task, returning an incomplete response while tool calls are still pending. The termination check is: if "Final answer:" in response.content[0].text: break. What is the root cause?

    A) The model sometimes includes "Final answer:" in intermediate reasoning before all tools complete. B) The max_tokens limit is cutting off the response before the model can finish. C) The tool results are not being appended to the conversation history. D) The model's temperature setting is too high, causing erratic behavior.

    Correct: A. Parsing natural language signals for loop termination is an anti-pattern. The model may include the phrase "Final answer:" while still planning tool calls. Use stop_reason == "end_turn" instead — it's Claude's deterministic signal that all tool calls are complete. Why not B: A max_tokens cutoff would produce a stop_reason of "max_tokens", not a clean exit triggered by matching the phrase. Why not C: If tool results weren't appended, the agent would fail on subsequent reasoning, not exit with a premature "Final answer:" match. Why not D: High temperature affects word choice variety but doesn't cause the model to insert specific control phrases like "Final answer:" at the wrong time. (Lab 1.1 Step 4)

    Q2 (Task 1.2). Your multi-agent research system produces reports that consistently cover only 2 of 5 relevant subtopics. Each subagent completes its assigned work correctly. Coordinator logs show it delegates narrow subtasks. What should you fix?

    A) Give the synthesis agent instructions to identify and flag coverage gaps. B) Broaden the coordinator's task decomposition to cover all relevant subtopics before delegating. C) Add more web search queries to each search subagent. D) Increase the context window for each subagent so they can find more information.

    Correct: B. The problem is at the coordinator level — it's decomposing too narrowly. Subagents execute their assignments correctly; the issue is what they were assigned. This matches Exam Sample Q7. Why not A: A synthesis agent can only flag gaps in what it receives — it can't generate research on subtopics that were never investigated. Why not C: More search queries per subagent deepens coverage of already-assigned subtopics but doesn't address the missing ones. Why not D: Larger context windows help subagents process more information but don't fix the coordinator's failure to assign all subtopics. (Lab 1.2)

    Q3 (Task 1.5). A customer support agent must block refunds over $500 and redirect to human escalation. Currently, the system prompt says "Do not process refunds above $500." In testing, the agent processes a $600 refund 3% of the time. What's the best fix?

    A) Add few-shot examples showing the agent refusing $600+ refunds. B) Implement a PreToolUse hook that intercepts process_refund calls and blocks amounts > $500 with a structured error redirecting to escalation. C) Reduce the model temperature to 0 for more deterministic behavior. D) Add "CRITICAL" emphasis to the system prompt instruction about the $500 limit.

    Correct: B. When business rules require 100% compliance, programmatic enforcement (hooks/gates) provides deterministic guarantees. Prompt-based approaches (A, C, D) still have a non-zero failure rate. This matches Exam Sample Q1's reasoning. Why not A: Few-shot examples improve probabilistic behavior but cannot guarantee 100% compliance — the 3% failure rate would shrink but not reach zero. Why not C: Temperature 0 makes output more deterministic in token selection but does not eliminate the possibility of the model ignoring instructions. Why not D: Emphasizing prompt instructions with "CRITICAL" is still a prompt-based approach and cannot provide the deterministic guarantee a financial rule requires. (Lab 1.5)

    Domain 2 Practice Questions

    Q4 (Task 2.1). Your agent has two tools: analyze_content and analyze_document. Users report that web search results are being processed by analyze_document instead of analyze_content. Both tools have similar descriptions. What's the most effective first step?

    A) Add a routing classifier to pre-select the correct tool based on input type. B) Consolidate both tools into a single analyze tool. C) Expand each tool's description to include input formats, example queries, when to use it, and when NOT to use it versus the other tool. D) Add 10 few-shot examples showing correct tool selection for each input type.

    Correct: C. Tool descriptions are the primary mechanism LLMs use for selection. Expanding descriptions to differentiate tools is the lowest-effort, highest-leverage fix. This matches Exam Sample Q2. Why not A: A routing classifier adds unnecessary complexity when the root cause is ambiguous tool descriptions — fix the descriptions first before adding infrastructure. Why not B: Consolidating tools removes useful specialization and creates an overly broad tool that may perform worse at both tasks. Why not D: Few-shot examples consume tokens and are a heavier intervention than simply clarifying tool descriptions, which is the more direct fix. (Lab 2.1)

    Q5 (Task 2.2). A subagent's database query times out. It returns {"error": "Operation failed"} to the coordinator. The coordinator can't determine whether to retry, use a backup, or proceed with partial results. What change enables intelligent recovery?

    A) Add automatic retry with exponential backoff inside the subagent. B) Return structured error context: failure type, attempted query, partial results, and suggested alternatives. C) Log the error and return an empty result set marked as successful. D) Propagate the exception to terminate the entire workflow.

    Correct: B. Structured error context gives the coordinator enough information to make recovery decisions. Generic errors (A's eventual output) hide context. Empty-as-success (C) silently suppresses failures. Full termination (D) is excessive. This matches Exam Sample Q8. Why not A: Automatic retry handles transient failures but still returns a generic error if retries exhaust, leaving the coordinator without context to choose alternative recovery strategies. Why not C: Returning an empty result marked as successful hides the failure entirely, causing the coordinator to proceed with missing data it believes is complete. Why not D: Terminating the entire workflow over a single subagent timeout is disproportionate when partial results or alternative queries could still produce a useful outcome. (Lab 2.2)

    Domain 3 Practice Questions

    Q6 (Task 3.3). Your codebase has test files spread throughout (e.g., Button.test.tsx next to Button.tsx). You want all tests to follow the same conventions regardless of location. What's the most maintainable approach?

    A) Create .claude/rules/ files with YAML frontmatter glob patterns like paths: ["**/*.test.tsx"]. B) Put conventions in the root CLAUDE.md under a "Testing" header. C) Create a .claude/skills/ skill for test generation with the conventions embedded. D) Place a CLAUDE.md file in every directory that contains test files.

    Correct: A. Path-specific rules with glob patterns automatically apply when editing matching files regardless of directory location. This is the only option that handles files spread across the codebase. This IS Exam Sample Q6. Why not B: Root CLAUDE.md applies globally to all files, not specifically to test files — it lacks the targeted activation that glob patterns provide. Why not C: Skills are invoked on-demand for specific tasks, not automatically applied when editing test files, so conventions would only apply when the skill is explicitly triggered. Why not D: Placing CLAUDE.md in every directory containing test files is unmaintainable and creates duplication that drifts out of sync as the codebase grows. (Lab 3.3)

    Q7 (Task 3.6). Your CI pipeline runs claude "Review this PR" but the job hangs indefinitely. What's the fix?

    A) Use the -p flag: claude -p "Review this PR" B) Set CLAUDE_HEADLESS=true environment variable. C) Redirect stdin: claude "Review this PR" < /dev/null D) Add --batch flag: claude --batch "Review this PR"

    Correct: A. The -p (--print) flag runs Claude Code in non-interactive mode. Options B, C, D reference non-existent features or workarounds. This IS Exam Sample Q10. Why not B: CLAUDE_HEADLESS=true is not a real Claude Code environment variable — there is no headless mode toggle via env vars. Why not C: Redirecting stdin from /dev/null is a generic Unix workaround that doesn't properly invoke Claude Code's non-interactive processing pipeline. Why not D: --batch is not a valid Claude Code flag — it doesn't exist in the CLI. (Lab 3.6)

    Domain 4 Practice Questions

    Q8 (Task 4.3). Your extraction pipeline uses tool_use with a JSON schema. Invoices are extracted correctly with no JSON syntax errors. However, line items sometimes don't sum to the stated total, and the model fills in made-up vendor IDs for documents that don't contain them. What should you add?

    A) Switch to a stricter JSON schema mode. B) Add custom semantic validation (cross-field checks) and make vendor_id nullable to prevent fabrication. C) Increase max_tokens so the model has more room to be precise. D) Add few-shot examples showing correct extraction.

    Correct: B. tool_use + JSON schema eliminates syntax errors but NOT semantic errors (wrong sums, fabricated values). Custom validation catches cross-field issues, and nullable fields prevent fabrication. Why not A: A stricter JSON schema mode only enforces structural rules (types, required fields) — it cannot validate that line items sum correctly or detect fabricated values. Why not C: Increasing max_tokens gives the model more output space but does not improve the accuracy of extracted values or prevent hallucinated vendor IDs. Why not D: Few-shot examples can improve extraction quality probabilistically but cannot guarantee cross-field consistency or prevent fabrication the way programmatic validation can. (Lab 4.3, Lab 4.4)

    Q9 (Task 4.5). Your manager wants to switch both a blocking pre-merge review and an overnight tech debt report to the Message Batches API for 50% cost savings. What's the correct evaluation?

    A) Batch both — the cost savings justify the change. B) Batch the tech debt report only; keep synchronous API for the pre-merge check. C) Keep both synchronous to avoid batch ordering issues. D) Batch both with a timeout fallback to synchronous.

    Correct: B. The Batch API has up to 24-hour processing with no latency SLA — unsuitable for blocking pre-merge checks. Ideal for overnight jobs. This IS Exam Sample Q11. Why not A: Batching both ignores that the pre-merge check is blocking — developers would wait up to 24 hours for a review that currently takes seconds. Why not C: Keeping both synchronous forfeits the 50% cost savings on the overnight report, which has no latency requirement and is a perfect batch candidate. Why not D: A timeout fallback adds complexity and still risks pre-merge delays — the Batch API offers no latency guarantees, so the fallback would trigger frequently, negating cost savings. (Lab 4.5)

    Domain 5 Practice Questions

    Q10 (Task 5.1). After a 15-turn customer support conversation, your agent says "your order total was approximately $150" when the actual total from turn 3 was $149.99. What pattern prevents this?

    A) Increase the context window to retain all prior messages. B) Extract transactional facts (amounts, dates, order IDs) into a persistent case facts block included in each prompt. C) Use progressive summarization to compress the conversation. D) Have the agent re-read all prior tool results before each response.

    Correct: B. Case facts blocks persist exact values outside summarized history. Progressive summarization (C) is the CAUSE of the problem — it compresses specific values into vague approximations. Why not A: The context window is likely already large enough to hold 15 turns — the issue is that exact values get lost during summarization, not that messages are being dropped. Why not C: Progressive summarization is what causes exact values like $149.99 to become approximations like "approximately $150" — it makes the problem worse, not better. Why not D: Re-reading all prior tool results before each response wastes tokens and doesn't scale as conversation length grows, while a case facts block achieves the same goal efficiently. (Lab 5.1)

    Q11 (Task 5.2). Your agent escalates 45% of cases to human agents, well above your 20% target. Logs show it escalates standard damage replacements while attempting to handle complex policy exceptions. What's the best fix?

    A) Add explicit escalation criteria with few-shot examples showing when to escalate vs resolve. B) Add sentiment analysis to only escalate frustrated customers. C) Have the agent self-report confidence and escalate below a threshold. D) Deploy a classifier trained on historical tickets.

    Correct: A. Explicit criteria with few-shot examples addresses the root cause: unclear decision boundaries. Sentiment (B) doesn't correlate with case complexity. Self-reported confidence (C) is poorly calibrated. A classifier (D) is over-engineered when prompting hasn't been tried. This matches Exam Sample Q3. Why not B: Customer sentiment doesn't determine case complexity — a calm customer can have a complex policy exception while a frustrated customer may have a simple replacement request. Why not C: LLMs are poorly calibrated at self-reporting confidence, and the agent is already confidently making wrong decisions, so a confidence threshold won't fix misclassified cases. Why not D: Training a classifier requires labeled historical data and infrastructure, making it over-engineered when the simpler fix of explicit criteria in the prompt hasn't been attempted yet. (Lab 5.2)

    Q12 (Task 5.6). Your synthesis agent combines findings from 3 research subagents. The final report says "market grew 14%" without citing which source, and a conflicting statistic from another source is dropped entirely. What's the fix?

    A) Give the synthesis agent access to the original sources for re-verification. B) Require subagents to output structured claim-source mappings that the synthesis agent must preserve and merge. C) Run two synthesis passes and compare outputs. D) Have each subagent also produce a summary alongside raw findings.

    Correct: B. Structured claim-source mappings force the synthesis agent to preserve attribution. Conflicting values should be annotated with both sources, not dropped. Why not A: Giving the synthesis agent access to original sources adds token cost and complexity without addressing the structural problem — it may still drop conflicting data without a required format. Why not C: Running two synthesis passes and comparing outputs may surface inconsistencies but doesn't solve the root cause of missing attribution and dropped conflicts in either pass. Why not D: Subagent summaries add redundant information alongside raw findings but don't enforce the structured attribution that prevents the synthesis agent from dropping or misattributing claims. (Lab 5.6)

    SCENARIO-BASED PRACTICE — EXAM FORMAT

    The real exam presents a scenario paragraph, then asks 3-5 questions within that scenario. These mini-scenarios simulate that format and cross-cut multiple domains — just like the real exam.

    Scenario A: Customer Support Resolution Agent

    You are building a customer support agent using the Claude Agent SDK. The agent has access to get_customer, lookup_order, process_refund, and escalate_to_human MCP tools. Your target is 80%+ first-contact resolution.

    A1. Production logs show the agent calls process_refund without first calling get_customer in 8% of cases, occasionally refunding the wrong account. The system prompt says "Always verify customer identity first." What's the most effective fix?

    A) Add few-shot examples showing the agent calling get_customer before every refund. B) Implement a programmatic prerequisite gate that blocks process_refund until get_customer returns a verified customer ID. C) Add "CRITICAL" to the system prompt instruction about verification. D) Reduce temperature to 0 for deterministic behavior.

    Correct: B. When compliance is required (financial operations), programmatic enforcement provides deterministic guarantees. Prompt-based approaches (A, C, D) all have non-zero failure rates. Why not A: Few-shot examples improve the model's tendency to call get_customer first but cannot guarantee it 100% of the time — an 8% failure rate on financial operations is unacceptable. Why not C: Adding "CRITICAL" emphasis is still a prompt-based approach that the model can occasionally ignore, leaving a non-zero risk of refunding the wrong account. Why not D: Temperature 0 makes token selection more deterministic but does not eliminate the possibility of skipping the verification step entirely. (Lab 1.4)

    A2. After a 20-turn conversation about a billing dispute, the agent says the disputed amount is "around $200" when the original tool result showed $199.47. What pattern prevents this?

    A) Increase the model's context window. B) Extract exact amounts, dates, and order IDs into a persistent case facts block included in every prompt. C) Have the agent re-read all prior tool results before each response. D) Use progressive summarization to compress the conversation.

    Correct: B. Case facts blocks persist exact values outside summarized history. Progressive summarization (D) is the CAUSE of the problem. Re-reading all tool results (C) wastes tokens. Larger context window (A) delays but doesn't prevent summarization loss. Why not A: A larger context window delays when summarization occurs but doesn't prevent exact values from eventually being approximated once summarization kicks in. Why not C: Re-reading all prior tool results before every response is token-expensive and doesn't scale — a case facts block achieves the same precision at a fraction of the cost. Why not D: Progressive summarization is precisely what causes exact values like $199.47 to become "around $200" — it compresses specifics into approximations. (Lab 5.1)

    A3. A customer says "I bought a competitor's product for $30 less — can you match that price?" Your refund policy covers returns and defective items but says nothing about competitor price matching. What should the agent do?

    A) Deny the request since it's not covered by the refund policy. B) Offer a 10% courtesy discount as a compromise. C) Escalate to a human agent because the policy is silent on this situation. D) Ask the customer to provide proof of the competitor's price before deciding.

    Correct: C. This is a policy gap — the policy doesn't address competitor price matching. The agent has no authority to act on something the policy doesn't cover. Denying (A) is wrong because the policy isn't denying it either — it's simply silent. Compromise (B) exceeds the agent's authority. Why not A: The policy doesn't deny price matching — it's silent on it, so denying the request is the agent making a policy decision it isn't authorized to make. Why not B: Offering a courtesy discount is inventing a policy that doesn't exist, exceeding the agent's authority to act only within defined guidelines. Why not D: Asking for proof implies the agent could approve a price match after verification, but no such policy exists — this delays escalation while implying authority the agent doesn't have. (Lab 5.2)

    Scenario B: CI/CD Pipeline with Code Review

    You are integrating Claude Code into your CI/CD pipeline to automate code reviews and generate test cases. The system must provide actionable feedback on pull requests while minimizing false positives.

    B1. Your CI job runs claude "Review this PR for security issues" but hangs indefinitely. Logs show Claude Code is waiting for interactive input. What's the fix?

    A) Set the CLAUDE_HEADLESS=true environment variable. B) Add the -p flag: claude -p "Review this PR for security issues" C) Redirect stdin from /dev/null. D) Add the --batch flag.

    Correct: B. The -p (--print) flag runs Claude Code in non-interactive mode — processes the prompt and exits. The other options reference non-existent features or workarounds. Why not A: CLAUDE_HEADLESS=true is not a valid Claude Code environment variable — no such headless mode exists. Why not C: Redirecting stdin from /dev/null is a generic Unix trick that doesn't properly engage Claude Code's non-interactive processing mode. Why not D: --batch is not a valid Claude Code CLI flag — it does not exist. (Lab 3.6)

    B2. A PR modifies 12 files. Your single-pass review produces detailed feedback for the first 3 files but superficial comments for the rest, with contradictory feedback — flagging a pattern as problematic in one file while approving identical code elsewhere. How should you restructure?

    A) Switch to a model with a larger context window. B) Require developers to split PRs into 3-4 files maximum. C) Split into per-file local analysis passes plus a separate cross-file integration pass. D) Run 3 independent reviews and only report issues found in at least 2 of 3.

    Correct: C. Per-file passes ensure consistent depth. A separate integration pass catches cross-file issues (data flow, interface contracts). Larger context (A) doesn't fix attention quality. Forcing small PRs (B) shifts burden to developers. Consensus filtering (D) suppresses real bugs. Why not A: A larger context window doesn't fix the attention degradation problem — the model still gives diminishing focus to later files regardless of available context. Why not B: Requiring developers to split PRs into 3-4 files shifts the burden to developers and doesn't address cross-file consistency issues that span the original change set. Why not D: Consensus filtering (reporting only issues found by 2 of 3 runs) suppresses real bugs that are intermittently detected, reducing recall for the sake of false-positive reduction. (Lab 4.6)

    B3. Your review produces accurate security findings but also flags 60% false positives in the "comment accuracy" category. Developers have started ignoring ALL review findings. What's the best immediate action?

    A) Add confidence scores and filter out low-confidence findings. B) Disable the "comment accuracy" category entirely, then improve its criteria separately. C) Add more few-shot examples for the comment accuracy category. D) Switch to a more capable model for better accuracy.

    Correct: B. Disabling the high-FP category immediately restores trust in the remaining accurate categories. Developers start reading findings again. Then iterate on the problematic category's criteria before re-enabling. Confidence scores (A) don't help when the model is confidently wrong. Why not A: Confidence scores are unreliable when the model is confidently wrong — a high-confidence false positive still passes the filter and erodes developer trust. Why not C: Adding few-shot examples may gradually improve the category but doesn't address the immediate trust crisis — developers are already ignoring all findings while you iterate. Why not D: Switching models is expensive and slow, and there's no guarantee a different model will perform better on this specific category without also improving the criteria. (Lab 4.1)

    PRACTICE EXAM — FULL 60-QUESTION ASSESSMENT

    This practice exam simulates the real certification exam. It uses 4 of the 6 possible scenarios, with questions distributed proportionally to domain weights.

    Instructions:

    • Answer all 60 questions — there is no penalty for guessing
    • Click "Show Answer" after each question to check your work
    • Passing score: 720/1000 (scaled) — aim for 43+ correct out of 60
    • Track your score by domain to identify weak areas

    Domain Distribution:

    • Domain 1: Agentic Architecture & Orchestration — 16 questions (27%)
    • Domain 2: Tool Design & MCP Integration — 11 questions (18%)
    • Domain 3: Claude Code Configuration & Workflows — 12 questions (20%)
    • Domain 4: Prompt Engineering & Structured Output — 12 questions (20%)
    • Domain 5: Context Management & Reliability — 9 questions (15%)

    SCENARIO 1: CUSTOMER SUPPORT RESOLUTION AGENT

    You are building a customer support resolution agent using the Claude Agent SDK. The agent handles high-ambiguity requests like returns, billing disputes, and account issues. It has access to your backend systems through custom MCP tools (get_customer, lookup_order, process_refund, escalate_to_human). Your target is 80%+ first-contact resolution while knowing when to escalate.

    Q1 (Task 1.1). Your customer support agent's agentic loop currently checks whether the assistant's response contains the phrase "I've completed your request" to decide when to stop iterating. In production, the agent sometimes terminates prematurely when it uses slightly different wording like "Your issue has been resolved." Other times it continues looping after completing the task because it phrases its response differently. What should you change about the loop termination logic?

    A) Add more phrase variations to the string-matching check, covering common completion phrasings. B) Replace the string-matching check with stop_reason inspection — continue when stop_reason is "tool_use" and terminate when it is "end_turn". C) Set a maximum iteration count of 10 and terminate when that limit is reached, regardless of completion status. D) Add a dedicated finish_task tool that the agent must call to signal completion explicitly.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The stop_reason field is the canonical mechanism for controlling agentic loop flow — "tool_use" means Claude wants to call another tool, and "end_turn" means it has finished reasoning and is ready to present its final response. This is deterministic and language-independent. Why not A: Adding more phrase variations is fragile and will always miss edge cases — it's solving a fundamentally wrong approach with more of the same approach. Why not C: Arbitrary iteration caps as the primary stopping mechanism can truncate legitimate multi-step workflows or waste iterations on completed tasks. Why not D: Adding a custom finish tool adds unnecessary complexity when stop_reason already provides this signal natively.

    Q2 (Task 1.1). You are debugging your customer support agent and notice that after calling get_customer, the agent's next turn doesn't reference any of the customer data that was returned. Examining your loop code, you find that you invoke the tool and check the stop_reason correctly, but you send the next API request with only the original conversation history. What is the most likely cause?

    A) The get_customer tool is returning data in a format Claude cannot parse. B) You are not appending the tool result to the conversation history before sending the next request, so Claude has no record of what the tool returned. C) The system prompt needs to instruct Claude to reference tool results in its reasoning. D) The context window is full and the tool result is being silently truncated.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. In an agentic loop, tool results must be appended to the conversation history (as a tool_result message) so the model can reason about them in the next iteration. If the result is never added, the model literally does not see it. Why not A: The tool returning unparseable data would cause errors, not silent omission — the model would at least acknowledge receiving something. Why not C: The model naturally references data in its context; the problem is the data was never placed in context. Why not D: Context truncation would affect all messages, not selectively omit a single tool result.

    Q3 (Task 1.2). Your customer support system has grown to handle multiple product lines, each with specialized policies. You have a coordinator agent that receives all incoming requests.
