Currently, it always routes every request through a sequential pipeline: first get_customer, then lookup_order, then a product-specialist subagent, then a resolution subagent. Metrics show that 40% of requests are simple FAQ questions that don't require order lookups or product specialists. What architectural change would most improve efficiency?

    A) Add a caching layer so repeated FAQ questions skip all subagents entirely. B) Redesign the coordinator to analyze query requirements and dynamically select which subagents to invoke based on complexity, skipping unnecessary steps for simple queries. C) Create a separate FAQ bot that handles simple questions, and route only complex requests to the coordinator. D) Run all subagents in parallel for every request and discard results from agents that weren't needed.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. A coordinator agent should analyze each query's requirements and dynamically decide which subagents to invoke rather than always routing through the full pipeline. For FAQ queries, the coordinator can respond directly without invoking order lookup or product specialist subagents. Why not A: A caching layer addresses repeated identical questions but doesn't solve the architectural problem of unnecessary pipeline steps for novel simple questions. Why not C: A separate FAQ bot creates a brittle routing boundary — questions that seem simple may actually need order context, and maintaining two systems increases complexity. Why not D: Running all subagents in parallel for every request wastes compute and latency for the 40% of simple requests, and introduces unnecessary failure points.

    Q4 (Task 1.3). Your coordinator agent delegates billing disputes to a billing subagent. The billing subagent needs the customer's account details, recent orders, and the specific complaint to investigate. Currently, the subagent is producing generic responses because it lacks context about the customer's situation. How should you fix the context passing?

    A) Give the billing subagent access to the get_customer and lookup_order tools so it can retrieve the information itself. B) Store the customer data in a shared database that both the coordinator and subagent can access. C) Include the complete customer details, relevant order data, and specific complaint directly in the billing subagent's prompt when spawning it via the Task tool. D) Have the coordinator write the customer context to a temporary file that the billing subagent reads on startup.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Subagents do not automatically inherit the coordinator's conversation history. Context must be explicitly provided in the subagent's prompt. Including the relevant customer data, order information, and complaint directly in the Task tool's prompt gives the subagent everything it needs to produce a contextualized response. Why not A: Giving the subagent redundant tool access means it would need to re-discover information the coordinator already has, increasing latency and token usage, and it wouldn't know which customer to look up without context anyway. Why not B: A shared database adds infrastructure complexity and still requires the subagent to know what to query. Why not D: File-based context passing adds unnecessary I/O complexity and race conditions when the prompt itself is the natural mechanism.

    Q5 (Task 1.4). Your customer support agent handles requests that involve multiple concerns — for example, "I want to return order #456 and also dispute the shipping charge on order #789." Production logs show the agent resolves the first concern but then presents a final response without addressing the second. What is the most effective approach to fix this?

    A) Add instructions to the system prompt telling the agent to always check if there are multiple concerns before responding. B) Implement a pre-processing step that splits multi-concern messages into separate tickets, each handled independently. C) Design the agent to decompose multi-concern requests into distinct items, investigate each using shared customer context, and synthesize a unified resolution that addresses all concerns before responding. D) Limit customers to one concern per message and prompt them to submit additional requests separately.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. The agent should decompose multi-concern requests into distinct items, investigate each in parallel using the shared customer context, and then synthesize a unified resolution. This preserves the customer experience while ensuring completeness. Why not A: Prompt instructions alone have a non-zero failure rate for ensuring coverage — the agent already "knows" it should handle all concerns but is failing to do so consistently. Why not B: Splitting into separate tickets destroys shared context (the customer is the same) and creates a fragmented experience requiring the customer to repeat information. Why not D: Restricting customers is a poor user experience that doesn't solve the underlying system limitation.

    Q6 (Task 1.4). Your agent processes refund requests. Business policy requires identity verification via get_customer before any financial operation. Despite clear system prompt instructions stating "Always verify customer identity before processing refunds," production logs show the agent skips verification in 8% of cases — particularly when customers provide order numbers upfront and sound frustrated. What change would most effectively guarantee compliance?

    A) Add few-shot examples showing the agent calling get_customer first, even when the customer volunteers order details and expresses urgency. B) Implement a programmatic prerequisite hook that blocks process_refund calls until get_customer has returned a verified customer ID in the current session. C) Increase the emphasis in the system prompt by adding "CRITICAL" and "MANDATORY" tags to the verification requirement. D) Log all refund requests and have a human review any that skipped verification, feeding corrections back as training data.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. When a specific tool sequence is required for compliance, programmatic enforcement provides deterministic guarantees. A hook that blocks process_refund until get_customer has completed eliminates the 8% failure rate entirely. Why not A: Few-shot examples improve probabilistic compliance but cannot achieve the 100% guarantee required for financial operations. Why not C: Adding emphasis keywords does not materially change LLM compliance rates — the model already understands the instruction; it's choosing to skip it under certain conditions. Why not D: Post-hoc human review catches violations after they occur but doesn't prevent them, and the damage (incorrect refund) is already done.

    Q7 (Task 1.5). Your agent calls multiple MCP tools that return dates in different formats: get_customer returns Unix timestamps (1672531200), lookup_order returns ISO 8601 strings ("2023-01-01T00:00:00Z"), and a shipping tool returns human-readable strings ("January 1, 2023"). The agent occasionally makes date comparison errors because it misinterprets formats. What is the best approach to fix this?

    A) Add instructions to the system prompt explaining each tool's date format and how to compare them correctly. B) Implement a PostToolUse hook that normalizes all date fields to a consistent ISO 8601 format before the agent processes the results. C) Modify all three backend services to return dates in the same format. D) Add a date_converter tool that the agent can call whenever it needs to compare dates.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. A PostToolUse hook intercepts tool results and transforms them before the model processes them. Normalizing heterogeneous date formats to a single standard eliminates comparison errors at the infrastructure level without relying on the model's arithmetic. Why not A: Prompt instructions for format conversion put the burden on the LLM to do reliable date math across formats, which is exactly the kind of task LLMs handle unreliably. Why not C: Modifying three backend services may not be feasible (they may serve other consumers) and is disproportionate effort for a client-side normalization problem. Why not D: Adding a converter tool increases latency with extra round trips and still relies on the model to recognize when conversion is needed.

    Q8 (Task 1.5). Your company policy caps automated refunds at $500. Above that threshold, a human agent must approve the refund. The support agent currently handles this through a system prompt instruction: "If the refund amount exceeds $500, use escalate_to_human instead of process_refund." In the past month, three refunds above $500 were processed automatically. What is the most effective fix?

    A) Add a dollar amount check in the system prompt with emphasized formatting and multiple reminders throughout the prompt. B) Implement a tool call interception hook that inspects process_refund calls, blocks any with amount > $500, and automatically redirects to escalate_to_human with the refund details. C) Remove the process_refund tool entirely and have all refunds go through human approval. D) Add a confirmation step where the agent asks the customer "Are you sure?" before processing refunds above $500.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. A tool call interception hook provides deterministic enforcement of business rules. Inspecting process_refund calls and blocking those exceeding $500 guarantees compliance regardless of what the model decides, then redirecting to escalate_to_human preserves the workflow. Why not A: The prompt already contains this instruction and fails 0.6% of the time — adding emphasis does not materially change compliance rates for business-critical rules. Why not C: Removing process_refund eliminates all automated refunds, including the vast majority under $500 that the agent handles correctly, destroying efficiency. Why not D: Asking the customer for confirmation doesn't enforce the policy — the customer will always say "yes" and the agent would still process the over-limit refund.

    Q9 (Task 2.1). Your agent has two tools with similar functionality: get_customer (retrieves customer profile by email or phone) and lookup_account (retrieves account details by account ID). Production logs show the agent calls get_customer when users provide account IDs, and calls lookup_account when users provide email addresses — the opposite of what's intended. Both tools have one-line descriptions: "Gets customer info" and "Gets account info." What is the most effective first step?

    A) Add few-shot examples to the system prompt showing correct tool selection for each input type. B) Expand each tool's description to clearly specify which input types it accepts, what it returns, example queries, and when to use it versus the other tool. C) Rename the tools to search_by_email_phone and search_by_account_id to make the distinction obvious from the name alone. D) Implement input validation in each tool that rejects incorrect identifier formats and returns an error message suggesting the correct tool.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Tool descriptions are the primary mechanism LLMs use for tool selection. When descriptions are minimal and similar ("Gets customer info" vs "Gets account info"), the model lacks context to differentiate. Expanding descriptions with input formats, example queries, and explicit boundary guidance is the highest-leverage, lowest-effort fix. Why not A: Few-shot examples add token overhead and don't fix the root cause — ambiguous descriptions will continue causing errors on novel query patterns not covered by examples. Why not C: Renaming helps but doesn't fully resolve the issue without also explaining expected inputs, outputs, and edge cases in the description. Why not D: Input validation is a useful safety net but reactive rather than proactive — the agent still wastes a round trip calling the wrong tool before getting corrected.

    Q10 (Task 2.2). Your get_customer tool currently returns a generic error string "Error: operation failed" for all failure modes — whether the customer email doesn't exist, the database is temporarily unavailable, or the API key has expired. The agent responds to all errors by telling the customer "I'm having trouble looking up your account, let me try again," leading to infinite retry loops on non-transient errors. How should you restructure the error responses?

    A) Return different HTTP status codes for each error type and have the agent interpret the codes. B) Return structured error metadata including errorCategory (transient/validation/permission), isRetryable boolean, and a human-readable description so the agent can make appropriate recovery decisions. C) Have the tool retry internally three times before returning any error, so the agent only sees persistent failures. D) Log all errors to a monitoring system and have a human operator intervene when errors occur.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Structured error metadata gives the agent the context it needs to make appropriate decisions: retry transient errors, ask the customer for different information on validation errors, and escalate on permission errors. The isRetryable flag directly prevents infinite retry loops on non-transient failures. Why not A: HTTP status codes are an implementation detail of the transport layer; MCP tools should return semantic error information using the isError flag pattern with structured content. Why not C: Internal retries help with transient failures but mask the error type from the agent, preventing appropriate handling of non-transient errors. Why not D: Human operator intervention doesn't scale and introduces significant latency for issues the agent could handle automatically with better error information.

    Q11 (Task 2.3). Your customer support agent currently has access to 16 tools including get_customer, lookup_order, process_refund, escalate_to_human, plus 12 internal analytics and reporting tools used by a separate admin dashboard. Production logs show the agent occasionally calls analytics tools during customer conversations, producing confusing responses. What should you do?

    A) Add instructions to the system prompt listing which tools are appropriate for customer conversations. B) Restrict the agent's tool set to only the 4 customer-facing tools (get_customer, lookup_order, process_refund, escalate_to_human), removing access to analytics and reporting tools entirely. C) Implement a pre-classifier that determines the request type and enables only relevant tools for each turn. D) Keep all 16 tools available but add "INTERNAL ONLY — do not use in customer conversations" to the analytics tool descriptions.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Giving an agent access to too many tools degrades tool selection reliability by increasing decision complexity. The agent should only have access to tools relevant to its role. Analytics tools belong on a separate admin agent, not the customer support agent. Why not A: Prompt instructions for tool filtering are probabilistic — with 16 tools available, the model will occasionally select the wrong one despite instructions. Why not C: A pre-classifier adds unnecessary infrastructure complexity when the simpler solution is removing irrelevant tools from the agent's scope. Why not D: Warning labels in descriptions still leave the tools available for selection, and the model may override or misinterpret the warnings.

    Q12 (Task 2.4). Your team wants to integrate a Jira MCP server so the support agent can create tickets for issues that need engineering follow-up. A teammate suggests building a custom MCP server that wraps the Jira REST API. What is the best approach?

    A) Build the custom MCP server as suggested — it gives you full control over the tool interface and error handling. B) Use an existing community Jira MCP server for the standard integration, reserving custom server development for team-specific workflows that community servers don't cover. C) Skip the MCP server entirely and have the agent call the Jira REST API directly using a bash tool. D) Build a lightweight proxy that translates MCP calls to Jira API calls, giving you control without building a full MCP server.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Community MCP servers for standard integrations like Jira have already solved common issues (authentication, pagination, error handling) and are maintained by the community. Custom servers should be reserved for team-specific workflows not covered by existing solutions. Why not A: Building a custom server for a standard integration duplicates effort and creates maintenance burden when community solutions already exist. Why not C: Calling REST APIs via bash bypasses the structured tool interface and error handling that MCP provides, making the integration fragile. Why not D: A proxy is essentially a custom MCP server with extra indirection — it has the same maintenance burden without the benefits of a community-maintained solution.

    Q13 (Task 5.1). Your support agent handles complex cases that span 15+ conversation turns. After turn 12, the agent starts giving contradictory information — telling the customer their refund was $47.50 when earlier in the conversation the confirmed amount was $52.30. Investigation reveals the agent is summarizing earlier turns and losing precise numerical values. What is the most effective fix?

    A) Increase the context window size to avoid any summarization of earlier turns. B) Extract transactional facts (amounts, dates, order numbers, statuses) into a persistent "case facts" block that is included in every prompt, outside the summarized conversation history. C) Instruct the agent to always scroll back through the full conversation before providing any numerical information. D) Add a reminder at the end of the system prompt to "always double-check amounts before quoting them to customers."

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Progressive summarization risks losing precise numerical values, dates, and other transactional facts. Extracting these into a structured "case facts" block that persists outside the summarized history ensures the agent always has access to accurate figures regardless of how many turns have been summarized. Why not A: Larger context windows are expensive and don't fundamentally prevent the attention degradation that occurs with very long conversations. Why not C: Instructing the agent to "scroll back" doesn't work in an API context — the conversation history is whatever is in the messages array, and summarized content is already lost. Why not D: A reminder to double-check doesn't help when the correct values have been lost from the summarized context — the agent can only reference what's in its current context.

    Q14 (Task 5.2). A customer contacts your agent about a price-matching request. Your company's policy document covers price adjustments for items found cheaper on your own website but says nothing about matching competitor prices. The agent attempts to process a competitor price match using the standard price adjustment tool, which fails. How should the agent handle this situation?

    A) Inform the customer that price matching is not available and close the case. B) Retry the price adjustment with different parameters to work around the tool failure. C) Escalate to a human agent because the policy is ambiguous on this specific request — the agent should not make policy decisions when the policy is silent. D) Apply the standard price adjustment policy and match the competitor's price, since the policy doesn't explicitly prohibit it.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. When policy is ambiguous or silent on a customer's specific request, the agent should escalate to a human who has authority to make policy decisions. Applying a policy beyond its stated scope (D) or refusing outright (A) both risk incorrect outcomes. Why not A: The policy doesn't say price matching is unavailable — it's silent on this case, which is different from an explicit prohibition. The agent shouldn't make policy interpretations. Why not B: Retrying with different parameters won't resolve a policy gap — the tool failure reflects a legitimate business constraint, not a technical error. Why not D: Extending a policy beyond its explicit scope risks authorizing actions the business didn't intend, which could have financial or legal consequences.

    Q15 (Task 5.2). A customer types "Just connect me to a real person." Your agent has already retrieved the customer's order and identified that the issue is a straightforward missing-item replacement that it can resolve in under a minute. What should the agent do?

    A) Explain that it has already identified the solution, resolve the issue, and then ask if the customer needs anything else. B) Immediately honor the customer's explicit request and escalate to a human agent without attempting further resolution. C) Ask the customer why they want to speak to a human and try to address their underlying concern first. D) Inform the customer that human agents are currently unavailable and offer to resolve the issue now.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. When a customer explicitly requests to speak to a human agent, the agent should honor that request immediately. Even if the issue is simple, the customer has made their preference clear. Attempting to override that preference damages trust. Why not A: Resolving the issue against the customer's stated preference is dismissive — the customer asked for a human, not a faster resolution from the bot. Why not C: Questioning the customer's request adds friction and can feel adversarial, especially when the customer is already frustrated enough to demand a human. Why not D: Fabricating excuses about human availability to force the customer to interact with the bot is deceptive and erodes trust.

    SCENARIO 3: MULTI-AGENT RESEARCH SYSTEM

    You are building a multi-agent research system using the Claude Agent SDK. A coordinator agent delegates to specialized subagents: one searches the web, one analyzes documents, one synthesizes findings, and one generates reports. The system researches topics and produces comprehensive, cited reports.

    Q16 (Task 1.1). Your research coordinator agent's loop terminates after the first subagent completes, even when additional subagents need to run. Debugging reveals the loop checks if the response contains any text content and terminates if it does, because the coordinator sometimes includes a brief status update ("Web search complete, now analyzing documents...") alongside its tool_use calls. What should you change?

    A) Instruct the coordinator to never include text alongside tool calls. B) Check stop_reason instead of text content — continue the loop when stop_reason is "tool_use" (regardless of accompanying text) and terminate only when stop_reason is "end_turn". C) Strip all text content from responses before checking for tool calls. D) Add a counter that ensures at least 4 iterations (one per subagent) before allowing termination.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The stop_reason field is the authoritative signal for loop control. A response with stop_reason "tool_use" means the model wants to execute tools, even if it also includes explanatory text. Checking for text content is an anti-pattern that breaks when the model includes status messages alongside tool calls. Why not A: Instructing the coordinator to suppress text is prompt-based and unreliable — models naturally include contextual text, and suppressing it reduces observability. Why not C: Stripping text content is a workaround that doesn't fix the root cause and destroys potentially useful coordination information. Why not D: A fixed iteration count is brittle — some research tasks may require 2 subagents while others require 6, and capping at 4 either wastes iterations or truncates necessary work.

    Q17 (Task 1.2). Your coordinator agent always invokes subagents in a fixed sequence: web search, then document analysis, then synthesis, then report generation — even for queries where some steps are unnecessary. For example, a query asking to "summarize the key findings from this uploaded PDF" still triggers a web search that returns irrelevant results. These irrelevant results then confuse the synthesis step. What architectural improvement would most effectively address this?

    A) Add a filtering step between web search and synthesis that removes irrelevant results. B) Design the coordinator to analyze query requirements and dynamically select which subagents to invoke, skipping unnecessary steps based on the query's needs. C) Give each subagent the ability to skip its own step if it determines the input is irrelevant. D) Create separate coordinator agents for different query types, each with a fixed pipeline appropriate to that type.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The coordinator should analyze each query's requirements and dynamically decide which subagents to invoke. For a "summarize this PDF" query, only document analysis and synthesis are needed — web search adds noise. This is the core role of a coordinator: intelligent task decomposition and delegation. Why not A: Filtering irrelevant results is a band-aid that still wastes the latency and cost of unnecessary web searches and may not catch all irrelevant content. Why not C: Individual subagents can't reliably determine relevance without the coordinator's broader query understanding, and this distributes coordination logic inappropriately. Why not D: Creating separate coordinators for each query type creates maintenance burden and requires an additional routing layer to select the right coordinator.

    Q18 (Task 1.2). Your coordinator decomposes the query "economic impact of remote work" into subtasks: "remote work salary data," "remote work productivity statistics," and "remote work technology costs." The final report covers only quantitative aspects, completely missing qualitative impacts like employee wellbeing, urban development, and environmental effects. What is the root cause?

    A) The synthesis agent is filtering out qualitative findings because its prompt emphasizes data-driven analysis. B) The web search agent is biased toward returning quantitative results. C) The coordinator's task decomposition is too narrow, focusing only on quantitative economic metrics and missing broader qualitative dimensions of the topic. D) The report generation agent is summarizing too aggressively and cutting qualitative sections.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. The coordinator's decomposition into only salary, productivity, and technology cost subtasks reveals overly narrow task decomposition. The subagents executed correctly within their assigned scope — the problem is that qualitative dimensions were never assigned. This is the coordinator's responsibility. Why not A: The synthesis agent works with what it receives; if no qualitative findings are provided, it can't synthesize them regardless of its prompt. Why not B: The web search agent searches for what it's told to search for; the queries themselves were narrow, not the search behavior. Why not D: The report generator can't cut content that was never produced by upstream agents.

    Q19 (Task 1.3). Your coordinator needs to invoke web search, document analysis, and a domain-expert subagent for a complex research query. Currently, it invokes them sequentially across three turns, adding 45 seconds of cumulative latency. The web search and document analysis subagents are independent of each other — neither needs the other's results. How can you reduce latency?

    A) Increase the timeout for each subagent to allow faster processing. B) Have the coordinator emit multiple Task tool calls for independent subagents in a single response, enabling parallel execution. C) Pre-cache results from common queries so subagents can skip their analysis. D) Combine the web search and document analysis subagents into a single agent that does both tasks.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Spawning parallel subagents by emitting multiple Task tool calls in a single coordinator response allows independent subagents to execute concurrently. Since web search and document analysis don't depend on each other, parallel execution can reduce the 45-second sequential latency to roughly the duration of the slowest single subagent. Why not A: Increasing timeouts doesn't reduce processing time — it just allows more time before failure, which is the opposite of the goal. Why not C: Pre-caching assumes predictable queries, which contradicts the open-ended nature of research tasks. Why not D: Combining agents into one eliminates parallelism since a single agent processes tasks sequentially, and it violates separation of concerns.

    Q20 (Task 1.3). Your synthesis subagent receives findings from the web search and document analysis agents but produces a generic report that doesn't reference specific data from either source. When you inspect the coordinator's Task tool call to the synthesis subagent, the prompt says: "Synthesize the research findings into a comprehensive report." What is the problem and how should you fix it?

    A) The synthesis subagent needs access to the web search and document analysis tools so it can retrieve the findings itself. B) The coordinator should store findings in a shared memory space that the synthesis subagent reads from. C) Include the complete findings from the web search and document analysis agents directly in the synthesis subagent's prompt, with structured data separating content from metadata (source URLs, document names, page numbers). D) Give the synthesis subagent a longer context window so it can process more information.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Subagent context must be explicitly provided in the prompt — subagents do not automatically inherit parent context. The coordinator must include the actual findings, using structured data formats that separate content from metadata (source URLs, document names) to preserve attribution for cited reports. Why not A: Giving the synthesis agent search tools violates separation of concerns and duplicates work already done by specialized agents. Why not B: Shared memory adds infrastructure complexity; the prompt is the natural and simplest mechanism for context passing in Agent SDK. Why not D: A longer context window doesn't help when the context is empty — the issue is that findings weren't included in the prompt at all.

    Q21 (Task 1.6). You need to research a broad topic with many potential subtopics. Your current approach has the coordinator generate all subtasks upfront before any research begins. The problem is that initial research often reveals important subtopics and connections that weren't apparent before investigation started, leading to incomplete coverage. What task decomposition strategy would address this?

    A) Have the coordinator generate more initial subtasks by casting a wider net during the planning phase. B) Use a fixed sequential pipeline that covers all possible subtopics in a predetermined order. C) Implement an iterative refinement approach where the coordinator evaluates synthesis output for coverage gaps after each round, re-delegates to search and analysis subagents with targeted queries, and re-invokes synthesis until coverage is sufficient. D) Let subagents autonomously decide to research additional subtopics they discover, without coordinator involvement.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Iterative refinement loops allow the coordinator to evaluate synthesis output for gaps and re-delegate with targeted queries. This adaptive approach discovers subtopics that emerge from initial research rather than trying to predict everything upfront. Why not A: Generating more initial subtasks is still a static decomposition — it can't anticipate subtopics that only become apparent after initial findings are analyzed. Why not B: A fixed sequential pipeline is even more rigid than the current approach and doesn't adapt to discovered information. Why not D: Letting subagents autonomously expand scope bypasses the coordinator's role in managing scope, observability, and preventing redundant work across agents.

    Q22 (Task 1.6). Your multi-agent system needs to analyze a research question that has both a well-understood quantitative component (gathering published statistics) and an open-ended qualitative component (analyzing expert opinions and emerging trends). What task decomposition pattern is most appropriate?

    A) Use prompt chaining for both components — define the full analysis sequence upfront. B) Use dynamic adaptive decomposition for both components — let the coordinator decide steps as findings emerge. C) Use prompt chaining for the quantitative component (predictable steps: gather data, validate sources, compile statistics) and dynamic adaptive decomposition for the qualitative component (explore expert opinions, follow emerging themes, iterate on gaps). D) Use a single subagent for both components to maintain consistent analysis context.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Different task types call for different decomposition patterns. Quantitative data gathering follows predictable steps well-suited to prompt chaining, while qualitative analysis requires adaptive investigation that discovers new threads during research. Matching the pattern to the task type maximizes both efficiency and coverage. Why not A: Prompt chaining for qualitative analysis constrains exploration to predetermined steps, likely missing emerging themes and expert viewpoints. Why not B: Dynamic decomposition for quantitative gathering adds unnecessary overhead for a straightforward sequence of known steps. Why not D: A single agent handling both loses the benefits of specialization and parallel execution.

    Q23 (Task 1.7). A researcher used your system yesterday to analyze market trends in renewable energy. Today they want to continue the research with a focus on policy implications, building on yesterday's findings. The original session generated extensive web search results and document analyses. What is the best approach for continuing the work?

    A) Resume the original session using --resume with the session name, so all prior context is preserved. B) Start a new session and include a structured summary of key findings from yesterday's research in the initial prompt, rather than resuming with stale tool results. C) Fork the original session using fork_session to explore policy implications as a separate branch. D) Re-run all of yesterday's queries to refresh the data before adding policy analysis.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Starting a new session with a structured summary of key findings is more reliable than resuming when prior tool results may be stale. Yesterday's web search results and document analyses consumed significant context but their raw outputs are less valuable than distilled findings. A fresh session with injected summaries gives the model clean context for the new research direction. Why not A: Resuming a session from yesterday means the context includes stale tool results (web pages may have changed, new sources may be available) that consume tokens without adding current value. Why not C: fork_session is designed for exploring divergent approaches from a shared analysis baseline within a session, not for continuing work across days with a new research direction. Why not D: Re-running all queries wastes time and cost when only the summarized findings are needed as context for the new research direction.

    Q24 (Task 2.1). Your system has two tools for content retrieval: analyze_content and analyze_document. The web search agent calls analyze_document when it should call analyze_content, and vice versa. Both tools have descriptions that include the phrase "analyzes content from various sources." What is the most effective fix?

    A) Add a routing table in the system prompt that maps source types to tools. B) Rename the tools and update descriptions to eliminate functional overlap — for example, rename analyze_content to extract_web_results with a description specific to web page processing, and clarify analyze_document for local file analysis. C) Remove one tool and have the remaining tool handle both use cases. D) Add input validation that rejects incorrect source types and suggests the correct tool.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Renaming tools and updating descriptions to clearly differentiate their purpose, expected inputs, and boundaries eliminates the ambiguity causing misrouting. Names like extract_web_results immediately signal the tool's scope, and updated descriptions reinforce the boundaries. Why not A: A routing table in the system prompt adds token overhead and is probabilistic — the model may not consistently consult it, especially as the prompt grows. Why not C: Removing a tool only works if both truly serve the same purpose; if they access different backends (web vs local files), consolidation may not be feasible or desirable. Why not D: Input validation is reactive — the wrong tool is still called, wasting a round trip before the error is caught.

    Q25 (Task 2.2). Your web search subagent encounters a timeout while querying an external API. It implements retry logic and, after exhausting 3 retries, returns the error to the coordinator. However, the coordinator treats the failure the same way it treats a successful query that returned no results — it proceeds without that data and doesn't flag any gap in the final report. What is the root cause?

    A) The coordinator needs better instructions for handling missing data. B) The subagent is not distinguishing between access failures (timeouts needing retry decisions) and valid empty results (successful queries with no matches) — both are returned in the same format. C) The coordinator should automatically retry any subagent that fails. D) The retry count should be increased from 3 to 5 to reduce the chance of failure.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The fundamental issue is that access failures and valid empty results are semantically different but returned identically. A timeout means "we couldn't check" while an empty result means "we checked and found nothing." The coordinator needs this distinction to annotate coverage gaps (timeout) versus confirmed absence (empty results) in the final report. Why not A: The coordinator can't make better decisions without better information — the problem is in the error reporting, not the coordinator's logic. Why not C: Automatic retries by the coordinator may help with transient failures but don't address the reporting ambiguity — the coordinator still won't know if the subagent's empty result means "failed" or "nothing found." Why not D: More retries may reduce failures but don't fix the semantic confusion between failure and empty results.

    Q26 (Task 2.5). You need to help your document analysis subagent understand a large codebase of research papers stored in a repository. The agent needs to find all papers that reference a specific methodology, then read relevant sections. The agent currently uses Read to open every file in the directory and scan for the methodology term, which is slow and consumes enormous context. What is the better approach?

    A) Use Glob to find all PDF/text files, then Read each one in sequence. B) Use Grep to search file contents for the methodology term across all papers, then use Read only on the matching files to load the relevant sections. C) Use Bash to run a find command and pipe it to grep for the methodology term. D) Pre-index all papers into a search database and query the database instead.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Grep is designed for searching file contents for patterns across a codebase. Using Grep to find matching files first, then Read to load only the relevant portions, builds understanding incrementally rather than reading everything upfront. This is the recommended pattern: start with Grep to find entry points, then use Read to follow up on specific files. Why not A: Glob finds files by name patterns, not by content — it can't search for a methodology term inside files. Reading every file wastes context on irrelevant papers. Why not C: The built-in Grep tool is preferred over running grep via Bash, as it's optimized for the agent environment with proper permissions and access. Why not D: A search database is a valid optimization but adds infrastructure not required when Grep already provides efficient content search across files.

    Q27 (Task 5.3). Your web search subagent fails due to an API rate limit. It returns a generic error: {"status": "error", "message": "Search unavailable"}. The coordinator has no information about what was searched, whether any partial results were obtained, or whether the failure is temporary. As a result, it simply skips the web search component entirely. How should you redesign the error propagation?

    A) Have the subagent retry indefinitely until the rate limit resets. B) Return structured error context including the failure type ("rate_limit"), the attempted query, any partial results obtained before the limit, and potential alternatives (e.g., "retry after 60 seconds" or "use cached results from similar query"). C) Have the coordinator always retry failed subagents exactly once before skipping them. D) Log the error to an external monitoring system and alert an engineer to manually re-run the query.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Structured error context gives the coordinator the information needed for intelligent recovery — it knows the failure is temporary (rate limit), what was attempted, what partial results exist, and what alternatives are available. This enables the coordinator to wait and retry, use partial results, or annotate the gap. Why not A: Indefinite retries block the entire pipeline and could run for an unknown duration while consuming resources. Why not C: A fixed single retry is better than nothing but doesn't leverage the rich context needed for intelligent recovery — a rate limit with a known reset time might warrant waiting, while a permanent failure should not be retried at all. Why not D: External monitoring adds latency and human dependency for a situation the system can handle programmatically with better error information.

    Q28 (Task 5.6). Your synthesis agent combines findings from web search and document analysis. Two credible sources provide conflicting statistics: one academic paper says "remote workers are 13% more productive" while a government report says "remote workers show no significant productivity difference." The synthesis agent currently picks one value and presents it as fact. How should you redesign the synthesis output?

    A) Have the synthesis agent pick the more recent source's value. B) Average the two values and present the average. C) Annotate the conflict with source attribution — present both values with their sources, methodological context, and publication dates, distinguishing well-established findings from contested ones. D) Omit the conflicting data point entirely to avoid presenting inaccurate information.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Conflicting statistics from credible sources should be annotated with source attribution rather than arbitrarily selecting one value. The synthesis output should preserve both values with their sources, note the methodological differences that may explain the discrepancy, and distinguish well-established from contested findings. Why not A: Recency doesn't determine accuracy — the older study may have better methodology. Arbitrarily selecting one value hides the complexity. Why not B: Averaging conflicting findings produces a meaningless number that neither source supports and misrepresents the state of research. Why not D: Omitting conflicting data produces an incomplete report and hides important nuance — disagreement among credible sources is itself a finding worth reporting.

    Q29 (Task 5.1). Your coordinator collects findings from four subagents and passes them as a combined block to the synthesis subagent. The synthesis agent consistently produces thorough analysis of findings from the first and last subagents but provides superficial treatment of findings from the middle two subagents. All four subagents produced equally detailed outputs. What is the most likely cause and fix?

    A) The middle subagents' findings are less relevant, so the synthesis agent correctly deprioritizes them. B) The synthesis agent has a context window limit and the middle findings are being truncated. C) This is the "lost in the middle" effect — models reliably process information at the beginning and end of long inputs but may miss middle sections. Place key findings summaries at the beginning and organize detailed results with explicit section headers. D) The synthesis agent needs more detailed instructions about treating all findings equally.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. The "lost in the middle" effect is a well-documented phenomenon where models attend more strongly to information at the beginning and end of long contexts. Placing key findings summaries at the top and using explicit section headers with clear structure helps mitigate position-based attention bias. Why not A: All four subagents produced equally detailed outputs — the superficial treatment correlates with position, not relevance. Why not B: If findings were truncated, the synthesis would reference incomplete data or mention missing sections, not provide superficial but coherent analysis. Why not D: Adding instructions doesn't address the underlying attention bias — the model isn't choosing to deprioritize middle content; it's a limitation of how attention works over long inputs.

    Q30 (Task 5.6). Your subagents return findings as plain text paragraphs. During synthesis, source attribution is frequently lost — the final report makes claims without citing which source they came from, and occasionally attributes findings to the wrong source. How should you restructure subagent output?

    A) Add instructions to the synthesis agent to carefully track which findings came from which source. B) Require subagents to output structured claim-source mappings (claim text, source URL, document name, relevant excerpt, publication date) that downstream agents must preserve through synthesis. C) Have the synthesis agent verify each claim by re-querying the original sources. D) Number each finding sequentially and have the synthesis agent reference findings by number.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Structured claim-source mappings make attribution a data structure rather than a natural language inference task. When subagents output claims with explicit source metadata, the synthesis agent can preserve and merge these mappings mechanically rather than trying to infer attribution from unstructured text. Why not A: Instructions alone don't fix the structural problem — when findings are interleaved in plain text, even a careful model will lose track of which source supports which claim. Why not C: Re-querying sources adds latency and cost, and the original source content was already retrieved by the search agent — the problem is preserving attribution, not re-verifying content. Why not D: Sequential numbering helps but is fragile — it requires the synthesis agent to maintain a lookup table mentally, which degrades as the number of findings increases.

    SCENARIO 5: CI/CD PIPELINE WITH CODE REVIEW

    You are integrating Claude Code into your CI/CD pipeline. The system runs automated code reviews, generates test cases, and provides feedback on pull requests. You need to design prompts that provide actionable feedback and minimize false positives.

    Q31 (Task 3.1). A new developer joins your team and reports that Claude Code gives them different coding style suggestions than the rest of the team. Upon investigation, you find that the senior developer who set up Claude Code placed all coding standards in ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md on their own machine. What is the problem and the fix?

    A) The senior developer's CLAUDE.md file is outdated and needs to be refreshed. B) User-level CLAUDE.md (~/.claude/CLAUDE.md) applies only to that user — it is not shared with teammates via version control. Move the coding standards to the project-level .claude/CLAUDE.md or root CLAUDE.md so they are checked into the repository. C) The new developer needs to copy the senior developer's CLAUDE.md to their own home directory. D) Add the coding standards to the CI/CD pipeline configuration instead of CLAUDE.md.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. User-level CLAUDE.md files in ~/.claude/ are personal to each developer and not shared via version control. Project-level configuration (.claude/CLAUDE.md or root CLAUDE.md) is committed to the repository and automatically available to everyone who clones it. Why not A: The file isn't outdated — it's in the wrong scope. Refreshing it doesn't solve the sharing problem. Why not C: Manually copying files between developers' machines is fragile, doesn't scale, and goes out of sync immediately when standards change. Why not D: CI/CD pipeline configuration serves a different purpose and doesn't affect Claude Code's behavior during interactive development.

    Q32 (Task 3.1). Your project has grown to include a large monolithic CLAUDE.md file with 400+ lines covering API conventions, testing standards, deployment procedures, security guidelines, and frontend patterns. Developers report that Claude sometimes ignores relevant guidelines, and the file is difficult to maintain because changes to one section risk breaking others. What is the most maintainable reorganization?

    A) Split the file into multiple sections with clear headers within the same CLAUDE.md to improve readability. B) Split the CLAUDE.md into focused topic-specific files in .claude/rules/ (e.g., testing.md, api-conventions.md, deployment.md) and use @import syntax where cross-references are needed. C) Create separate CLAUDE.md files in each subdirectory for the conventions relevant to that area. D) Move the less-frequently-used guidelines to a wiki and reference the wiki URL in CLAUDE.md.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The .claude/rules/ directory is designed for organizing topic-specific rule files as an alternative to a monolithic CLAUDE.md. This approach makes each file independently maintainable, reduces irrelevant context loaded per session, and enables path-specific scoping with YAML frontmatter. The @import syntax supports cross-references when needed. Why not A: Better headers improve readability but don't reduce the context loaded per session — all 400+ lines are still included regardless of what the developer is working on. Why not C: Subdirectory CLAUDE.md files scope by directory location, which doesn't map well to cross-cutting concerns like testing standards that apply to files throughout the project. Why not D: Claude Code cannot access wiki URLs during operation — guidelines must be in local configuration files to be effective.

    Q33 (Task 3.2). Your CI/CD pipeline needs a reusable code review workflow that produces structured JSON output. The review should run in isolation so its verbose analysis output doesn't pollute the main session context. You want this available to all developers via the repository. Where and how should you configure it?

    A) Create a slash command in .claude/commands/ with the review instructions. B) Create a skill in .claude/skills/ with a SKILL.md file that includes context: fork in the frontmatter to run in an isolated sub-agent context, and allowed-tools to restrict tool access during review. C) Add the review logic to the project-level CLAUDE.md as a conditional instruction. D) Create a separate script that invokes Claude Code via the -p flag with the review prompt.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Skills in .claude/skills/ with SKILL.md files support frontmatter configuration including context: fork for isolation (preventing verbose output from polluting the main conversation) and allowed-tools for restricting tool access. This is purpose-built for reusable workflows that need isolation and controlled tool access. Why not A: Slash commands in .claude/commands/ don't support context: fork for isolation or allowed-tools restrictions — they run in the main session context. Why not C: CLAUDE.md is for always-loaded universal standards, not on-demand workflow invocations. Conditional logic in CLAUDE.md is fragile and always consumes context tokens. Why not D: A separate script works for CI but isn't available as an on-demand developer workflow, and loses the benefits of skill frontmatter configuration.

    Q34 (Task 3.3). Your codebase has React components, Python API handlers, and Terraform infrastructure files. You want Claude to automatically apply different coding conventions when working on each type of file. Test files (*.test.tsx, *.test.py) are spread throughout the codebase alongside the code they test. What is the best configuration approach?

    A) Create a single CLAUDE.md at the root with all conventions, organized by section headers. B) Create separate CLAUDE.md files in the src/components/, src/api/, and infrastructure/ directories. C) Create rule files in .claude/rules/ with YAML frontmatter glob patterns — e.g., paths: ["/*.tsx"] for React conventions, paths: ["/.py"] for Python conventions, paths: ["terraform/**/"] for infrastructure rules, and paths: ["**/.test."] for testing conventions. D) Create custom slash commands for each file type that developers invoke before working on that type of code.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Rule files in .claude/rules/ with YAML frontmatter paths fields containing glob patterns provide automatic, conditional convention loading based on file type regardless of directory location. This is essential for test files spread throughout the codebase — paths: ["**/.test."] matches all test files regardless of where they live. Why not A: A single CLAUDE.md loads all conventions for every file, wasting context on irrelevant rules and increasing the chance Claude ignores relevant ones. Why not B: Subdirectory CLAUDE.md files can't handle test files spread across multiple directories — each test file would need a CLAUDE.md in its parent directory. Why not D: Manual slash command invocation relies on developers remembering to run them and doesn't provide automatic convention loading.

    Q35 (Task 3.4). Your CI pipeline needs to handle two types of code review tasks: (1) reviewing a single-file bug fix with a clear stack trace showing exactly which line caused a null pointer exception, and (2) reviewing a proposed microservices migration plan that involves restructuring 30+ files across 6 services. Which approach should you use for each task?

    A) Use plan mode for both tasks to ensure thorough analysis. B) Use direct execution for both tasks to minimize latency in the CI pipeline. C) Use direct execution for the single-file bug fix (clear scope, straightforward fix) and plan mode for the microservices migration (complex, multi-file, multiple valid approaches, architectural decisions). D) Use plan mode for the bug fix to ensure correctness, and direct execution for the migration to get results faster.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Direct execution is appropriate for well-scoped changes with clear solutions — a single-file bug fix with an obvious stack trace doesn't need exploration. Plan mode is designed for complex tasks with architectural implications, multiple valid approaches, and multi-file changes — exactly what a microservices migration requires. Why not A: Plan mode for a simple bug fix adds unnecessary overhead when the problem and solution are already clear. Why not B: Direct execution on a 30+ file migration risks costly rework when dependencies and architectural decisions aren't explored first. Why not D: This is exactly backwards — simple tasks need direct execution, complex tasks need planning.

    Q36 (Task 3.5). Your CI pipeline generates test cases for new code. The generated tests compile and pass, but senior developers report the tests are "trivial" — they test only the happy path and don't cover edge cases, error conditions, or integration points. You've tried adding the instruction "Generate comprehensive tests including edge cases" but the results are still shallow. What is the most effective next step?

    A) Switch to a more capable model that generates better tests by default. B) Provide 2-3 concrete input/output examples showing the type of edge case tests you expect — for instance, an example test that handles null inputs, boundary values, and concurrent access patterns — so Claude can generalize the pattern. C) Add a second pass where Claude reviews its own generated tests for completeness. D) Have Claude generate 3x more tests and let the team delete the trivial ones.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Concrete input/output examples are the most effective way to communicate expected transformations when prose descriptions ("comprehensive," "edge cases") are interpreted inconsistently. Showing 2-3 specific examples of the quality and type of tests you expect lets Claude generalize the pattern to new code. Why not A: Switching models is expensive and slow, with no guarantee of improvement when the issue is unclear expectations rather than model capability. Why not C: Self-review within the same session is limited because the model retains its reasoning context and is less likely to question its own decisions. Why not D: Generating more trivial tests doesn't produce better tests — it produces more work for the team to sift through.

    Q37 (Task 3.5). You are iterating on Claude Code's output for a data migration script. The script handles most cases correctly but produces incorrect results for rows with null values in the "email" column — it inserts the string "null" instead of a database NULL. You've described the issue in prose but Claude keeps producing the same incorrect behavior. What approach is most likely to fix it?

    A) Add "IMPORTANT: Handle null values correctly" to the system prompt in bold and caps. B) Provide a specific test case with example input (a row with email = null) and expected output (database NULL, not the string "null"), so Claude can see exactly what correct behavior looks like. C) Ask Claude to explain how it handles null values, then correct its understanding. D) Rewrite the migration script yourself and have Claude review your solution.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. When natural language descriptions produce inconsistent results, providing specific test cases with concrete input and expected output is the most effective technique. Showing Claude exactly what null handling should look like eliminates ambiguity and enables test-driven iteration — Claude can run the test, see it fail, and fix its implementation. Why not A: Emphasis formatting doesn't materially change LLM behavior — the model already understands the instruction but is implementing it incorrectly due to ambiguity about what "correct" null handling means in this context. Why not C: Getting Claude to explain its reasoning may provide insight but doesn't guarantee it will fix the implementation without a concrete example of correct behavior. Why not D: Rewriting the script yourself defeats the purpose of using Claude for code generation and doesn't help Claude learn the correct pattern for future iterations.

    Q38 (Task 3.6). Your CI pipeline runs Claude Code for automated code review, but the job hangs indefinitely in the CI runner. Logs show Claude Code is waiting for interactive input. What is the correct fix?

    A) Set the CLAUDE_CI=true environment variable before running the command. B) Add the -p (--print) flag to run Claude Code in non-interactive mode: claude -p "Review this PR for security issues". C) Redirect stdin from /dev/null to prevent interactive prompts. D) Add the --no-interactive flag to the Claude Code command.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The -p (or --print) flag is the documented way to run Claude Code in non-interactive mode. It processes the prompt, outputs the result to stdout, and exits without waiting for user input — exactly what CI/CD pipelines require. Why not A: CLAUDE_CI is not a documented environment variable for Claude Code. Why not C: Redirecting stdin is a Unix workaround that doesn't properly address Claude Code's command syntax and may produce unexpected behavior. Why not D: --no-interactive is not a valid Claude Code flag.

    Q39 (Task 3.6). Your CI pipeline runs automated code reviews on every PR. After a developer pushes a fix addressing review findings, the pipeline runs again and posts duplicate comments about issues that were already fixed. How should you prevent this?

    A) Skip the review on subsequent commits if the first review was already posted. B) Include prior review findings in context when re-running reviews after new commits, and instruct Claude to report only new or still-unaddressed issues. C) Compare the new findings against the previous findings and filter out duplicates in post-processing. D) Only run reviews on the first commit in a PR and skip all subsequent commits.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Including prior review findings in context lets Claude see what was already flagged and determine whether those issues were addressed by the new commits. Instructing it to report only new or still-unaddressed issues prevents duplicates while still catching new problems. Why not A: Skipping reviews on subsequent commits means new issues introduced by the fix commit would go undetected. Why not C: Post-processing duplicate detection is fragile — findings may be worded differently even when describing the same issue, leading to missed deduplication. Why not D: Skipping reviews on later commits is even worse than option A — it ignores all new code pushed after the first commit.

    Q40 (Task 3.6). You want your CI pipeline to produce structured JSON output from Claude Code's review so you can post findings as inline PR comments. How should you configure the output?

    A) Parse Claude Code's natural language output with a regex to extract findings. B) Use --output-format json with --json-schema to enforce a specific structured output format that includes file path, line number, severity, and finding description. C) Have Claude Code write its findings to a JSON file, then read the file in a subsequent pipeline step. D) Use the Claude API directly instead of Claude Code for structured output.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The --output-format json and --json-schema CLI flags are designed for enforcing structured output in CI contexts. This produces machine-parseable JSON that matches your schema, enabling automated posting as inline PR comments. Why not A: Regex parsing of natural language output is fragile and will break when the model's output format varies even slightly. Why not C: Writing to an intermediate file adds complexity and failure points when Claude Code natively supports structured output on stdout. Why not D: Using the Claude API directly loses Claude Code's built-in file access, CLAUDE.md context, and tool capabilities that make code review effective.

    Q41 (Task 4.1). Your CI code review pipeline has a "comment accuracy" category that flags comments which don't match the code's actual behavior. However, developers report this category produces so many false positives that they've started ignoring ALL review findings — even the accurate ones from other categories like security and bug detection. What is the most effective immediate action?

    A) Add confidence scores to each finding and filter out low-confidence results. B) Disable the "comment accuracy" category entirely to restore trust in the remaining accurate categories, then improve its criteria separately before re-enabling it. C) Add more few-shot examples for the comment accuracy category to improve its precision. D) Reduce the severity of comment accuracy findings from "error" to "warning" so developers take them less seriously.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. When a high-FP category undermines confidence in accurate categories, the immediate priority is restoring trust. Disabling the problematic category lets developers start reading findings again. Then improve its criteria and re-enable it once precision is acceptable. Why not A: Confidence scores are unreliable when the model is confidently wrong — a high-confidence false positive still passes the filter and continues eroding trust. Why not C: Few-shot examples may gradually improve accuracy but don't address the immediate trust crisis — developers are already ignoring all findings while you iterate. Why not D: Reducing severity doesn't reduce the volume of false positives — developers still see noise that dilutes their attention to genuine issues.

    Q42 (Task 4.1). Your code review prompt says "Flag any issues you find, being conservative and only reporting high-confidence findings." Despite this instruction, the review still produces many false positives, particularly around intentional code patterns your team uses (like feature flags implemented as empty catch blocks). What change would most effectively improve precision?

    A) Change "conservative" to "very conservative" and add "minimize false positives." B) Replace the vague instruction with specific criteria: define which issues to report (bugs with clear impact, security vulnerabilities) and which patterns to skip (empty catch blocks for feature flags, intentional no-ops marked with comments), using concrete code examples. C) Add a post-processing filter that removes findings matching known false-positive patterns. D) Have developers rate each finding as correct or incorrect and fine-tune the model on the feedback.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. General instructions like "be conservative" fail to improve precision because they don't tell the model which specific patterns are acceptable. Writing specific review criteria with concrete code examples defining what to flag versus skip gives the model the judgment framework it needs. Why not A: Adding more emphasis to vague instructions doesn't improve precision — "very conservative" is no more actionable than "conservative" for the model. Why not C: Post-processing filters are reactive and require maintaining a growing list of patterns, rather than teaching the model to make correct judgments upfront. Why not D: Fine-tuning requires significant infrastructure, labeled data, and ongoing maintenance — it's a disproportionate response when prompt improvements haven't been tried.

    Q43 (Task 4.2). Your CI test generation produces tests that compile and pass but cover only obvious scenarios. You want Claude to generate tests for subtle edge cases like race conditions, boundary values, and error recovery paths. Adding the instruction "include edge cases" hasn't changed the output quality. What approach will most effectively improve test variety?

    A) Generate tests in multiple passes, with each pass targeting a specific category (happy path, boundary, error, concurrency). B) Provide 2-4 few-shot examples of high-quality edge case tests from your codebase, showing the reasoning for why each edge case matters — for example, a test that catches an off-by-one error at array boundaries, with a comment explaining the scenario. C) Increase the temperature to produce more creative test variations. D) Have Claude first analyze the code for potential failure modes, then generate tests targeting those specific modes.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Few-shot examples are the most effective technique for achieving consistently formatted, actionable output when instructions alone produce inconsistent results. Showing concrete examples of the quality and type of edge case tests you expect — with reasoning about why each matters — enables the model to generalize the judgment pattern to novel code. Why not A: Multiple passes can improve coverage but don't address the quality problem — each pass may still produce shallow tests without examples demonstrating what "good edge case tests" look like. Why not C: Higher temperature increases randomness but doesn't improve judgment about which edge cases matter — it's more likely to produce nonsensical tests than thoughtful ones. Why not D: Analyzing failure modes first is a reasonable approach but doesn't address the output quality issue — the model may identify failure modes correctly but still generate shallow tests for them.

    Q44 (Task 4.3). Your CI pipeline needs Claude Code to produce structured review findings in a specific JSON format: {file, line, severity, issue, suggested_fix}. Currently the pipeline parses Claude's natural language output with a regex, which breaks frequently. What is the most reliable approach?

    A) Improve the regex to handle more output variations. B) Use --output-format json with --json-schema specifying the exact schema ({file, line, severity, issue, suggested_fix}) so Claude Code produces guaranteed schema-compliant structured output. C) Add detailed instructions to the prompt specifying the JSON format and include 5 examples. D) Have Claude output XML instead of JSON for easier parsing.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Using --output-format json with --json-schema enforces structured output at the system level, eliminating JSON syntax errors and guaranteeing schema compliance. This is the purpose-built mechanism for CI contexts requiring machine-parseable output. Why not A: Improving regexes is an arms race — the model's natural language output will always have variations that break pattern matching. Why not C: Prompt-based JSON formatting is probabilistic — even with examples, the model may occasionally deviate from the format or produce invalid JSON syntax. Why not D: XML is harder to parse than JSON and equally susceptible to formatting inconsistencies when generated via natural language instructions.

    Q45 (Task 4.6). Your CI pipeline runs a single Claude Code pass to review a PR that modifies 18 files across your payment processing module. The review produces detailed, accurate feedback for the first few files but gives superficial comments for later files. It also flags a validation pattern as incorrect in one file while approving the identical pattern in another file within the same PR. How should you restructure the review?

    A) Increase the context window to give the model more attention capacity for all 18 files. B) Split the review into focused per-file local analysis passes (examining each file individually) plus a separate cross-file integration pass (examining data flow between files), then merge the findings. C) Run the same single-pass review three times and take the majority vote on each finding. D) Require developers to split large PRs into smaller submissions before review.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Splitting into per-file passes plus cross-file integration passes directly addresses attention dilution. Individual file analysis ensures consistent depth and avoids contradictory findings, while the integration pass catches cross-file data flow issues that per-file analysis would miss. Why not A: Larger context windows don't solve attention quality issues — the model can hold more information but still processes it unevenly. Why not C: Majority voting suppresses real findings that are only caught intermittently and doesn't fix the root cause of inconsistent attention. Why not D: Shifting burden to developers doesn't improve the review system and may not be feasible for changes that legitimately span many files.

    Q46 (Task 4.6). Your CI pipeline generates test cases and then uses the same Claude session to review whether the generated tests are adequate. The review consistently rates the generated tests as "comprehensive and well-structured," but human reviewers find the tests miss obvious edge cases. What is the problem and the fix?

    A) The review criteria need to be more specific about what constitutes comprehensive test coverage. B) The same Claude session that generated the tests retains its reasoning context, making it less likely to question its own decisions. Use a second independent Claude instance (without the generator's reasoning context) to review the generated tests. C) Increase the temperature during the review step to encourage more critical analysis. D) Add a checklist of specific edge cases the review should verify.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Self-review within the same session is limited because the model retains reasoning context from generation. It already "decided" these tests were good and is unlikely to question that decision. An independent review instance without prior reasoning context provides unbiased assessment. Why not A: More specific criteria help but don't fully address the self-review bias — the model will still apply criteria more leniently to its own output. Why not C: Higher temperature adds randomness but doesn't address the systematic bias of self-review — the model may produce a different but equally uncritical review. Why not D: A checklist is useful but still subject to self-review bias — the model may check off items it believes it covered without genuinely re-evaluating.

    Q47 (Task 4.2). Your code review pipeline produces findings with inconsistent formatting. Sometimes findings include file paths and line numbers; other times they're vague descriptions without location information. You've tried detailed instructions specifying the format (file, line, issue, severity, suggestion) but the output remains inconsistent. What should you add?

    A) A post-processing step that rejects findings without complete location information. B) 2-4 few-shot examples showing the exact output format you expect for different types of findings — including the file path, line number, issue description, severity level, and suggested fix in a consistent structure. C) A JSON schema that enforces the output structure. D) A template with placeholder values that Claude fills in for each finding.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Few-shot examples are the most effective technique for achieving consistently formatted output when detailed instructions alone produce inconsistent results. Showing 2-4 concrete examples of correctly formatted findings (with location, issue, severity, and fix) demonstrates the expected format more reliably than describing it. Why not A: Post-processing rejection discards potentially valuable findings rather than fixing the formatting problem at the source. Why not C: A JSON schema via tool_use is also effective but the question asks about adding to the existing prompt-based approach; few-shot examples are the most impactful addition to improve consistency. Why not D: Templates with placeholders tend to produce formulaic output where the model fills in blanks mechanically rather than providing thoughtful analysis.

    SCENARIO 6: STRUCTURED DATA EXTRACTION

    You are building a structured data extraction system using Claude. The system extracts information from unstructured documents, validates output using JSON schemas, and maintains high accuracy. It must handle edge cases gracefully and integrate with downstream systems.

    Q48 (Task 3.1). Your data extraction system processes documents from multiple departments: legal contracts, medical records, and financial reports. Each document type has different extraction rules and validation criteria. You want Claude Code operators in each department to have their own extraction conventions applied automatically when working on their document types, without loading irrelevant rules from other departments. What configuration approach is best?

    A) Create a single CLAUDE.md at the project root with all department rules and let Claude infer which apply. B) Create rule files in .claude/rules/ with YAML frontmatter path scoping — e.g., paths: ["legal//*"] for legal extraction rules, paths: ["medical//*"] for medical rules — so rules load only when editing matching files. C) Create separate CLAUDE.md files in each department's directory. D) Use environment variables to toggle between department rule sets.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Rule files in .claude/rules/ with YAML frontmatter path scoping automatically load the correct conventions based on file path. Legal rules load only when working on legal documents, medical rules for medical documents, etc. This reduces irrelevant context and ensures department-specific conventions are applied deterministically. Why not A: Loading all department rules for every file wastes context tokens and increases the chance Claude applies wrong-department conventions. Why not C: Subdirectory CLAUDE.md files work for simple cases but don't support cross-cutting concerns and lack the flexibility of glob pattern matching. Why not D: Environment variables require manual toggling and aren't tied to the file being edited.

    Q49 (Task 3.4). Your extraction system encounters a document in an unexpected format that the current extraction pipeline can't handle. You need to explore the document structure, understand its layout, and design a new extraction approach before implementing it. Should you use plan mode or direct execution?

    A) Direct execution — start extracting and adjust based on errors. B) Plan mode — explore the document structure, understand the layout patterns, and design an extraction approach before implementing it. C) Direct execution with comprehensive upfront instructions specifying how to handle the unknown format. D) It doesn't matter — both modes produce the same result for extraction tasks.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Plan mode is designed for tasks requiring exploration before commitment. An unknown document format requires understanding the structure, identifying patterns, and choosing an appropriate extraction strategy — exactly the kind of investigation where planning prevents costly rework. Why not A: Starting extraction without understanding the format leads to errors and wasted iterations as you discover unexpected patterns mid-implementation. Why not C: You can't write comprehensive instructions for a format you don't yet understand — this assumes knowledge you don't have. Why not D: Plan mode and direct execution serve fundamentally different purposes; plan mode is specifically valuable for exploration tasks.

    Q50 (Task 3.6). Your extraction system needs to process 5,000 invoices overnight for a weekly financial audit. The results are reviewed the next morning. Your manager proposes using real-time synchronous API calls for each invoice. How should you evaluate this proposal?

    A) Agree — synchronous calls ensure each extraction completes before the next begins, maintaining data integrity. B) Use the Message Batches API instead — it offers 50% cost savings and is designed for non-blocking, latency-tolerant workloads like overnight batch processing, while synchronous calls should be reserved for blocking workflows. C) Use synchronous calls but parallelize them across multiple threads for speed. D) Process invoices synchronously during the day when API rates are lower.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. The Message Batches API offers 50% cost savings and is designed for exactly this use case: non-blocking, latency-tolerant workloads with no immediate user waiting for results.
