Overnight processing with next-morning review is the ideal batch API scenario. Synchronous calls are appropriate for blocking workflows where users wait for results. Why not A: Sequential synchronous processing of 5,000 invoices is unnecessarily expensive and slow for a non-blocking overnight task. Why not C: Parallelized synchronous calls still cost twice as much as batch processing and add infrastructure complexity for managing threads and rate limits. Why not D: Time-of-day doesn't affect API pricing, and daytime processing contradicts the overnight use case.

    Q51 (Task 3.2). Your extraction team needs a custom command that runs an extraction workflow with specific validation steps. Different team members want slightly different validation strictness. How should you structure this?

    A) Create a single command in .claude/commands/ that accepts a strictness parameter. B) Create the base command in .claude/commands/ for team-wide availability via version control, and let individual developers create personal variants with different validation settings in ~/.claude/commands/ with different names. C) Create multiple versions of the command in .claude/commands/ with names like extract-strict and extract-lenient. D) Add validation strictness as a CLAUDE.md configuration parameter.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Project-scoped commands in .claude/commands/ are shared via version control, ensuring the team has a consistent baseline. Personal variants in ~/.claude/commands/ allow individuals to customize without affecting teammates, which is the correct pattern for user-specific preferences. Why not A: Parameter-based commands add complexity and may not cover all variation dimensions each developer wants. Why not C: Multiple command variants in the shared directory clutter the project and require consensus on naming, when the variations are personal preferences. Why not D: CLAUDE.md is for always-loaded standards, not per-invocation command parameters.

    Q52 (Task 4.3). Your extraction system needs to extract invoice data (vendor, amount, date, line_items) from unstructured documents. Currently, you instruct Claude to "output the data as JSON" in the prompt, but you frequently get invalid JSON (missing quotes, trailing commas) that crashes your downstream parser. What is the most reliable fix?

    A) Add examples of valid JSON in the prompt to improve formatting consistency. B) Add a JSON validation step that fixes common syntax errors before parsing. C) Define an extraction tool with a JSON schema (vendor: string, amount: number, date: string, line_items: array) and use tool_use with forced tool selection to guarantee schema-compliant structured output. D) Use a regex-based parser that's more tolerant of formatting variations.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Tool use with JSON schemas is the most reliable approach for guaranteed schema-compliant structured output. It eliminates JSON syntax errors entirely by having the model fill in schema-defined fields rather than generating free-form JSON text. Forced tool selection ensures the extraction tool is always called. Why not A: Few-shot examples improve consistency but don't eliminate JSON syntax errors — the model can still produce invalid JSON occasionally. Why not B: A JSON fixer is a band-aid that may introduce errors when "fixing" ambiguous syntax, and doesn't guarantee the output matches your expected schema structure. Why not D: A tolerant parser may accept invalid JSON but can't guarantee the parsed data matches your expected fields and types.

    Q53 (Task 4.3). Your extraction tool schema requires a "category" field for classifying invoice types. You defined it as an enum with values ["services", "goods", "subscription"]. In production, the system encounters consulting invoices that don't fit these categories. Claude forces them into "services," which is close but causes downstream routing errors. How should you modify the schema?

    A) Add "consulting" to the enum values. B) Remove the enum constraint and make category a free-text string field. C) Add an "other" enum value paired with a "category_detail" string field where the model can describe the actual category when none of the predefined values fit. D) Change the field to optional so the model can skip it when uncertain.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Adding an "other" enum value with a companion "category_detail" field provides extensibility while maintaining the benefits of enum constraints for known categories. The model uses "other" + detail when it encounters novel categories, giving downstream systems both a signal that manual review may be needed and a description for routing. Why not A: Adding specific values reactively is unsustainable — you'll need to update the enum every time a new invoice type appears. Why not B: Free-text strings eliminate the standardization benefits of enums and produce inconsistent values ("Services," "services," "Professional Services") that break downstream logic. Why not D: Making the field optional means you lose category information entirely for edge cases, rather than capturing the model's best description.

    Q54 (Task 4.4). Your extraction pipeline processes vendor invoices. Validation catches that the sum of line item amounts ($450 + $225 + $125 = $800) doesn't match the stated total ($850) on the invoice. The system retries the extraction, but it produces the same result. How should you handle this?

    A) Accept the extracted total since it matches the document. B) Average the two values and use that as the total. C) Design the extraction to capture both "calculated_total" (sum of line items) and "stated_total" (what the document says), flag the discrepancy with a "conflict_detected" boolean, and route to human review rather than retrying — the information isn't wrong, the source document is inconsistent. D) Retry with a more explicit prompt that says "ensure line items sum to the total."

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Retries are ineffective when the inconsistency exists in the source document itself — retrying will produce the same faithful extraction. Instead, capture both values (calculated vs stated total), flag the conflict, and route to human review for resolution. This is a semantic validation issue, not an extraction error. Why not A: Blindly accepting the stated total ignores a real discrepancy that may indicate a billing error or data entry mistake. Why not B: Averaging produces a number that doesn't appear in the source document and masks the conflict. Why not D: Instructing "ensure they sum correctly" would cause the model to fabricate line items or modify the stated total to force consistency, rather than faithfully extracting what the document actually says.

    Q55 (Task 4.4). Your extraction system processes medical records. Some records don't include a patient's blood type, but your schema has blood_type as a required field. The model fabricates plausible blood types (usually "O+") to satisfy the required constraint. How should you fix this?

    A) Add instructions saying "do not guess blood types." B) Make the blood_type field optional (nullable) in the schema so the model can return null when the information is absent from the source document, rather than fabricating values to satisfy a required field. C) Add a validation step that checks if the extracted blood type matches a known database. D) Add a confidence score for the blood_type field and filter out low-confidence extractions.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. When source documents may not contain certain information, schema fields should be optional (nullable). A required field forces the model to produce a value even when none exists in the source, leading to fabrication. Making it nullable allows the model to honestly return null for absent information. Why not A: Instructions help but don't override the schema constraint — if the field is required, the model must provide a value, creating a conflict between the instruction and the schema. Why not C: Validation against a database catches wrong values but doesn't prevent fabrication or address the root cause — the field shouldn't be required for documents that may not contain it. Why not D: Confidence scores on fabricated values are meaningless — the model may be "confident" in its fabrication because it's the most common blood type.

    Q56 (Task 4.5). You need to process 10,000 contracts for a quarterly compliance audit. Results must be ready within 30 hours of submission. The Message Batches API has a processing window of up to 24 hours. How should you plan the batch submission?

    A) Submit all 10,000 contracts in a single batch 30 hours before the deadline. B) Submit the batch with a 6-hour buffer (at least 30 hours before the deadline) to guarantee the 30-hour SLA given the 24-hour batch processing window, and plan to resubmit any failed documents by custom_id with modifications. C) Submit contracts one at a time using synchronous API calls to ensure sequential processing. D) Split into 10 batches of 1,000 contracts each and submit them in parallel.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. With a 24-hour batch processing window and a 30-hour SLA, you need buffer time for handling failures. Submitting 6 hours before the deadline allows 24 hours for batch processing plus 6 hours for resubmitting failed documents (identified by custom_id) with appropriate modifications. Why not A: Submitting exactly 30 hours before leaves zero buffer — if any documents fail, you can't resubmit within the deadline since a second batch could take another 24 hours. Why not C: Synchronous processing of 10,000 contracts is prohibitively expensive (no 50% batch discount) and time-consuming. Why not D: Splitting into smaller batches doesn't reduce total processing time (each still has up to 24-hour window) and adds complexity without benefit.

    Q57 (Task 5.5). Your extraction system achieves 97% overall accuracy on your test set. Management wants to fully automate all extractions without human review. Before agreeing, what validation should you perform?

    A) Run the system on a larger test set to confirm the 97% holds. B) Analyze accuracy by document type and field to verify consistent performance across all segments — aggregate accuracy may mask poor performance on specific document types or fields that could cause systematic downstream errors. C) Compare accuracy against a competitor's system to validate the benchmark. D) Increase the confidence threshold to 99% to further reduce errors.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Aggregate accuracy metrics can mask poor performance on specific document types or fields. A system that's 99% accurate on standard invoices but 60% accurate on handwritten receipts has a 97% aggregate if most documents are standard invoices — but the handwritten receipt errors could cause significant downstream problems. Field-level and document-type analysis reveals these hidden weaknesses. Why not A: A larger test set may confirm the aggregate number without revealing per-segment performance gaps. Why not C: Competitor comparison is irrelevant to whether the system is accurate enough for full automation — you need to validate your own system's performance across all segments. Why not D: Increasing the threshold filters out more extractions for human review but doesn't address the question of whether the high-confidence extractions are actually accurate across all document types.

    Q58 (Task 5.5). Your extraction system has been running at high accuracy for three months. You've reduced human review from 100% to only reviewing extractions where the model reports low confidence. A product manager suggests eliminating human review entirely since the system hasn't had significant errors recently. What is the right approach?

    A) Agree — three months of good performance demonstrates reliability. B) Implement stratified random sampling of high-confidence extractions for ongoing error rate measurement and novel pattern detection, rather than eliminating review entirely. C) Keep the low-confidence review threshold but lower it further to reduce review volume. D) Switch to reviewing a fixed random 5% sample regardless of confidence.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Stratified random sampling of high-confidence extractions catches novel error patterns that confidence-based routing misses. New document formats, regulatory changes, or data drift can introduce errors the model is confidently wrong about. Ongoing sampling is the safety net that enables confident automation. Why not A: Past performance doesn't guarantee future accuracy — new document types, vendor format changes, or regulatory updates can introduce novel error patterns at any time. Why not C: Lowering the confidence threshold reduces review volume but still only reviews low-confidence extractions, missing errors in high-confidence ones. Why not D: Fixed random sampling is better than no review but unstratified sampling may undersample rare document types where errors are more likely.

    Q59 (Task 5.4). Your extraction system requires operators to explore large document repositories to understand new document formats before configuring extraction pipelines. During an extended exploration session analyzing 200+ legal documents, the operator notices Claude starts giving inconsistent answers — referencing "typical contract patterns" rather than specific clauses discovered earlier in the session. Using /compact doesn't fully resolve the issue because key structural findings from early exploration are lost in summarization. What is the most effective approach?

    A) Start a new session every 30 minutes to avoid context degradation. B) Have the operator maintain a scratchpad file recording key structural findings (document types, field locations, formatting patterns) discovered during exploration, and reference the scratchpad for subsequent questions to counteract context degradation. C) Increase the context window size to avoid the need for compaction. D) Use a database to store all explored documents and query it instead of relying on Claude's context.

    Show Answer

    Correct: B. Context degradation in extended sessions causes models to lose specific findings discovered earlier and revert to generic pattern knowledge. Maintaining a scratchpad file that records key findings provides persistent state across context boundaries — the operator can reference it in subsequent questions to recall specific structural details without relying on the model's degraded context. Why not A: Restarting every 30 minutes loses all accumulated understanding and forces repeated re-exploration, making the process extremely inefficient. Why not C: Larger context windows are expensive and delay rather than prevent degradation — the underlying issue is attention quality over very long contexts, not capacity. Why not D: A database stores raw documents but doesn't capture the analytical findings (patterns, structural insights, field location mappings) that the operator needs to reference during ongoing exploration.

    Q60 (Task 5.6). Your extraction system processes financial documents from multiple sources. Two annual reports for the same company show different revenue figures: one says "$4.2 billion" and the other says "$3.8 billion." Your synthesis step currently picks the figure from whichever source it processes last. How should you redesign this?

    A) Always use the figure from the most recent report. B) Flag the discrepancy and reject both values until a human resolves it. C) Complete the extraction with both values included, annotated with source attribution and publication dates, so the consuming system can determine whether the difference reflects a revision, different fiscal periods, or different accounting methods — rather than arbitrarily selecting one. D) Average the two values as the best estimate.

    Show Answer

    Correct: C. Conflicting values from credible sources should be preserved with attribution rather than arbitrarily selected. Including both values with source names, publication dates, and context allows downstream systems or human reviewers to determine the reason for the discrepancy — it may reflect a restatement, different fiscal year definitions, or different accounting standards. Why not A: Recency doesn't determine accuracy — a more recent report might contain a revised figure, or it might report a different fiscal period. The system can't make this determination without context. Why not B: Rejecting both values blocks processing entirely and forces human intervention for every discrepancy, which is disproportionate when the discrepancy may have a simple explanation. Why not D: Averaging produces a meaningless number that no source supports and masks the actual data.

    EXAM ANSWER PATTERNS — CHEAT SHEET

    When you see these patterns in exam questions, this is the likely correct answer:

    Pattern 1: Compliance / Reliability

    "Agent sometimes skips a step" or "12% failure rate on a required sequence" → Programmatic enforcement (gates, hooks). NOT prompt-based. NOT few-shot.

    Pattern 2: Wrong Tool Selected

    "Agent calls the wrong tool" or "tools have similar descriptions" → Expand tool descriptions (purpose, inputs, outputs, when-to-use, when-NOT-to-use). NOT routing classifier. NOT consolidation.

    Pattern 3: Wrong Escalation Decisions

    "Escalates easy cases, handles hard ones" or "poor first-contact resolution" → Explicit escalation criteria + few-shot examples. NOT sentiment analysis. NOT confidence scores.

    Pattern 4: Review Quality Degrades on Large PRs

    "Inconsistent depth" or "contradictory findings across files" → Multi-pass review (per-file local + cross-file integration). NOT bigger model. NOT require smaller PRs.

    Pattern 5: CI Pipeline Hangs

    "Job hangs" or "waiting for interactive input" → -p flag for non-interactive mode. NOT env vars. NOT stdin redirect.

    Pattern 6: Cost Optimization

    "Reduce API costs" with a mix of blocking and non-blocking workflows → Batch API for non-blocking only (overnight reports). Keep synchronous for blocking (pre-merge checks).

    Pattern 7: Extracted Data Has Wrong Values

    "Schema validates but values are wrong" or "fabricated data" → Custom semantic validation + nullable fields. Schema catches syntax, NOT semantics.

    Pattern 8: Context Loss in Long Conversations

    "Agent forgets exact amounts" or "approximates specific values" → Case facts block persisting exact values. NOT just bigger context window.

    Pattern 9: Error Messages Don't Help Recovery

    "Coordinator can't decide whether to retry" or "generic error" → Structured error context (failure type, attempted query, partial results, alternatives).

    Pattern 10: Subagent Coverage Gaps

    "Report only covers X, missing Y and Z" → Fix coordinator task decomposition (too narrow). NOT fix downstream agents.

    Pattern 11: Convention Files for Cross-Directory Patterns

    "Test files spread throughout codebase" or "conventions by file type not directory" → .claude/rules/ with YAML frontmatter glob patterns. NOT directory-level CLAUDE.md files.

    Pattern 12: Self-Review Misses Issues

    "Same instance generated and reviewed" or "review misses subtle bugs" → Independent review instance (fresh context, no reasoning attachment). NOT self-review. NOT extended thinking.

    Remember the core thesis:

    • Deterministic compliance → programmatic (gates, hooks, schema enforcement)
    • Probabilistic guidance → prompts (few-shot, explicit criteria, system instructions)
    • Know which situation demands which approach. That's the whole exam.

    EXAM DAY QUICK REFERENCE

    Exam Format

    • All multiple choice — one correct answer, three plausible distractors
    • No penalty for guessing — answer every question
    • Passing score: 720 out of 1,000 (scaled)
    • 4 of 6 scenarios are presented (randomly selected)

    Domain Weights

    • Domain 1: Agentic Architecture & Orchestration — 27%
    • Domain 2: Tool Design & MCP Integration — 18%
    • Domain 3: Claude Code Configuration & Workflows — 20%
    • Domain 4: Prompt Engineering & Structured Output — 20%
    • Domain 5: Context Management & Reliability — 15%

    The 6 Scenarios

    1. Customer Support Agent → Domains 1, 2, 5
    2. Code Generation with Claude Code → Domains 3, 5
    3. Multi-Agent Research System → Domains 1, 2, 5
    4. Developer Productivity → Domains 2, 3, 1
    5. CI/CD Pipeline → Domains 3, 4
    6. Structured Data Extraction → Domains 4, 5

    Distractor Patterns — What the Wrong Answers Look Like

    • "Improve the system prompt" → when programmatic enforcement is needed
    • "Add confidence scores" → when explicit criteria with few-shot is correct
    • "Use a bigger model / larger context" → when multi-pass or trimming is correct
    • "Self-review" → when an independent review instance is needed
    • "Resume session" → when context is stale and a fresh start is better
    • "Generic error string" → when structured error context is needed
    • "Fix downstream agents" → when the coordinator's decomposition is too narrow
    • "Routing classifier" → when better tool descriptions are the first step

    The One Rule That Matters

    Deterministic guarantees = programmatic solutions (gates, hooks, schema). Probabilistic guidance = prompts (few-shot, criteria, system instructions). If compliance is required, it must be programmatic. If guidance is sufficient, use prompts. Every exam question traces back to this distinction.
